<p><b>Napoléon Bonaparte</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/iː/ or /ɪ/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="/ən/: 'on' in 'button'">ən</span></span> <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/ɑːr/: 'ar' in 'far'">ɑːr</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span></span>/</a></span></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> <small>French:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[napɔleɔ̃ bɔnapaʁt]</a></span>; 15 August 1769 – 5 May 1821) was a <a href="/wiki/French_Military" class="mw-redirect" title="French Military">French military</a> and <a href="/wiki/Political_leader" class="mw-redirect" title="Political leader">political leader</a> who rose to prominence during the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a> and led <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_Bonaparte%27s_battle_record" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleon Bonaparte's battle record">several successful campaigns</a> during the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolutionary_Wars" title="French Revolutionary Wars">French Revolutionary Wars</a>. As <b>Napoleon I</b>, he was <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_the_French" title="Emperor of the French">Emperor of the French</a> from 1804 until 1814, and again briefly in 1815 (during the <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Days" title="Hundred Days">Hundred Days</a>). Napoleon dominated European and global affairs for more than a decade while leading France against a series of coalitions in the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>. He won most of these wars and the vast majority of his battles, building a <a href="/wiki/First_French_Empire" title="First French Empire">large empire</a> that ruled over continental Europe before its final collapse in 1815. One of the greatest commanders in history, his wars and campaigns are studied at military schools worldwide. Napoleon's political and cultural legacy has endured as one of the most celebrated and controversial leaders in <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_world" title="History of the world">human history</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Roberts.2C_Andrew_2014_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roberts.2C_Andrew_2014-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>He was born <b>Napoleone di Buonaparte</b> (<small>Italian:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Italian" title="Help:IPA/Italian">[napoleˈoːne di bwɔnaˈparte]</a></span>) in <a href="/wiki/Corsica" title="Corsica">Corsica</a>, to a relatively modest family from the minor nobility. When the Revolution broke out in 1789, Napoleon was serving as an artillery officer in the French army. Seizing the new opportunities presented by the Revolution, he rapidly rose through the ranks of the military, becoming a general at age 24. The <a href="/wiki/French_Directory" title="French Directory">Directory</a> eventually gave him command of the <a href="/wiki/Army_of_Italy_(France)" title="Army of Italy (France)">Army of Italy</a> after he suppressed a <a href="/wiki/13_Vend%C3%A9miaire" title="13 Vendémiaire">revolt against the government</a> from royalist insurgents. At age 26, he began his <a href="/wiki/Italian_campaigns_of_the_French_Revolutionary_Wars" title="Italian campaigns of the French Revolutionary Wars">first military campaign</a> against the Austrians and their Italian allies—winning virtually every battle, conquering the Italian Peninsula in a year, and becoming a national hero. In 1798, he led a <a href="/wiki/French_campaign_in_Egypt_and_Syria" title="French campaign in Egypt and Syria">military expedition to Egypt</a> that served as a springboard to political power. He engineered a <a href="/wiki/Coup_of_18_Brumaire" title="Coup of 18 Brumaire">coup in November 1799</a> and became <a href="/wiki/French_Consulate" title="French Consulate">First Consul</a> of the Republic. His ambition and public approval inspired him to go further, and in 1804 he became the first <i>Emperor of the French</i>. Intractable differences with the British meant that the French were facing a <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Third_Coalition" title="War of the Third Coalition">Third Coalition</a> by 1805. Napoleon shattered this coalition with decisive victories in the <a href="/wiki/Ulm_Campaign" title="Ulm Campaign">Ulm Campaign</a> and a historic triumph over <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Empire" title="Austrian Empire">Austria</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Austerlitz" title="Battle of Austerlitz">Battle of Austerlitz</a>, which led to the elimination of the thousand-year-old <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>. In 1806, the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Fourth_Coalition" title="War of the Fourth Coalition">Fourth Coalition</a> took up arms against him because <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Prussia</a> became worried about growing French influence on the continent. Napoleon quickly defeated Prussia at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Jena%E2%80%93Auerstedt" title="Battle of Jena–Auerstedt">battles of Jena and Auerstedt</a>, then marched the <a href="/wiki/Grande_Arm%C3%A9e" title="Grande Armée">Grand Army</a> deep into <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a> and annihilated the Russians in June 1807 at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Friedland" title="Battle of Friedland">Battle of Friedland</a>. France then forced the defeated nations of the Fourth Coalition to sign the <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_Tilsit" title="Treaties of Tilsit">Treaties of Tilsit</a> in July 1807, bringing an uneasy peace to the continent. Tilsit signified the high watermark of the French Empire. In 1809, the Austrians and the British challenged the French again during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Fifth_Coalition" title="War of the Fifth Coalition">War of the Fifth Coalition</a>, but Napoleon solidified his grip over Europe after triumphing at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Wagram" title="Battle of Wagram">Battle of Wagram</a> in July.</p>
<p>Hoping to extend the <a href="/wiki/Continental_System" title="Continental System">Continental System</a> and choke off British trade with the European mainland, Napoleon invaded <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberia</a> and declared his brother <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Bonaparte" title="Joseph Bonaparte">Joseph</a> the King of Spain in 1808. The Spanish and the Portuguese revolted with British support. The <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">Peninsular War</a> lasted six years, featured extensive <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla_warfare" title="Guerrilla warfare">guerrilla warfare</a>, and ended in victory for the Allies. The Continental System caused recurring diplomatic conflicts between France and its client states, especially Russia. Unwilling to bear the economic consequences of reduced trade, the Russians routinely violated the Continental System and enticed Napoleon into another war. The French launched a major <a href="/wiki/French_invasion_of_Russia" title="French invasion of Russia">invasion of Russia</a> in the summer of 1812. The resulting campaign witnessed the collapse of the Grand Army and the destruction of Russian cities, and inspired a renewed push against Napoleon by his enemies. In 1813, Prussia and Austria joined Russian forces in a <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Sixth_Coalition" title="War of the Sixth Coalition">Sixth Coalition</a> against France. A lengthy military campaign culminated in a large Allied army defeating Napoleon at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Leipzig" title="Battle of Leipzig">Battle of Leipzig</a> in October 1813. The Allies then <a href="/wiki/1814_campaign_in_France" class="mw-redirect" title="1814 campaign in France">invaded France</a> and captured Paris in the spring of 1814, forcing Napoleon to abdicate in April. He was exiled to the island of <a href="/wiki/Elba" title="Elba">Elba</a> near Rome and the <a href="/wiki/Bourbon_dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Bourbon dynasty">Bourbons</a> were <a href="/wiki/Bourbon_restoration" class="mw-redirect" title="Bourbon restoration">restored to power</a>. However, Napoleon escaped from Elba in February 1815 and took control of France once again. The Allies responded by forming a <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Seventh_Coalition" class="mw-redirect" title="War of the Seventh Coalition">Seventh Coalition</a>, which defeated Napoleon at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Waterloo" title="Battle of Waterloo">Battle of Waterloo</a> in June. The British exiled him to the remote island of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Helena" title="Saint Helena">Saint Helena</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">South Atlantic</a>, where he died six years later at the age of 51.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Napoleon had an extensive and powerful influence on the modern world, bringing liberal reforms to the numerous territories that he conquered and controlled, such as the <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries" title="Low Countries">Low Countries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, and large parts of modern <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>. He implemented fundamental liberal policies in France and throughout Western Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[note 1]</a></sup> His legal achievement, the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Code" title="Napoleonic Code">Napoleonic Code</a>, has influenced the legal systems of more than 70 nations around the world. British historian <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Roberts_(historian)" title="Andrew Roberts (historian)">Andrew Roberts</a> stated, "The ideas that underpin our modern world—meritocracy, equality before the law, property rights, religious toleration, modern secular education, sound finances, and so on—were championed, consolidated, codified and geographically extended by Napoleon. To them he added a rational and efficient local administration, an end to rural banditry, the encouragement of science and the arts, the abolition of feudalism and the greatest codification of laws since the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Roman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Fall of the Roman Empire">fall of the Roman Empire</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins_and_education">Origins and education</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carlo_Buonaparte.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Half-length portrait of a wigged middle-aged man with a well-to-do jacket. His left hand is tucked inside his waistcoat." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Carlo_Buonaparte.jpg/170px-Carlo_Buonaparte.jpg" width="170" height="229" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Carlo_Buonaparte.jpg/255px-Carlo_Buonaparte.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Carlo_Buonaparte.jpg/340px-Carlo_Buonaparte.jpg 2x" data-file-width="580" data-file-height="782" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carlo_Buonaparte.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Napoleon's father <a href="/wiki/Carlo_Buonaparte" title="Carlo Buonaparte">Carlo Buonaparte</a> was <a href="/wiki/Corsica" title="Corsica">Corsica</a>'s representative to the court of <a href="/wiki/Louis_XVI_of_France" title="Louis XVI of France">Louis XVI of France</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Napoleon was born on 15 August 1769, to <a href="/wiki/Carlo_Buonaparte" title="Carlo Buonaparte">Carlo Maria di Buonaparte</a> and <a href="/wiki/Letizia_Ramolino" title="Letizia Ramolino">Maria Letizia Ramolino</a>, in his family's ancestral home <a href="/wiki/Casa_Buonaparte" class="mw-redirect" title="Casa Buonaparte">Casa Buonaparte</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ajaccio" title="Ajaccio">Ajaccio</a>, the capital of the island of Corsica. He was their fourth child and third son. This was a year after the island was transferred to France by the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Republic of Genoa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup> He was christened <i>Napoleone di Buonaparte</i>, probably named after an uncle (an older brother who <a href="/wiki/Necronym" title="Necronym">did not survive infancy</a> was the first of the sons to be called Napoleone). In his 20s, he adopted the more French-sounding <i>Napoléon Bonaparte</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-dwyerxv_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dwyerxv-16">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[note 2]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Corsican Buonapartes were descended from minor <a href="/wiki/Nobility_of_Italy" title="Nobility of Italy">Italian nobility</a> of <a href="/wiki/Tuscany" title="Tuscany">Tuscan</a> origin, who had come to Corsica from <a href="/wiki/Liguria" title="Liguria">Liguria</a> in the 16th century.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[17]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paoli.png" class="image"><img alt="Head and shoulders portrait of a white-haired, portly, middle-aged man with a pinkish complexion, blue velvet coat, and a ruffle" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Paoli.png/170px-Paoli.png" width="170" height="198" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Paoli.png/255px-Paoli.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0c/Paoli.png 2x" data-file-width="305" data-file-height="356" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paoli.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The nationalist Corsican leader <a href="/wiki/Pasquale_Paoli" title="Pasquale Paoli">Pasquale Paoli</a>; portrait by <a href="/wiki/Richard_Cosway" title="Richard Cosway">Richard Cosway</a>, 1798</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>His father <i>Nobile</i> Carlo Buonaparte was an attorney, and was named Corsica's representative to the court of <a href="/wiki/Louis_XVI_of_France" title="Louis XVI of France">Louis XVI</a> in 1777. The dominant influence of Napoleon's childhood was his mother, Letizia Ramolino, whose firm discipline restrained a rambunctious child.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[18]</a></sup> Napoleon's maternal grandmother had married into the Swiss <a href="/wiki/Faesch" title="Faesch">Fesch</a> family in her second marriage, and Napoleon's uncle, the cardinal <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Fesch" title="Joseph Fesch">Joseph Fesch</a>, would fulfill a role as protector of the Bonaparte family for some years.</p>
<p>He had an elder brother, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Bonaparte" title="Joseph Bonaparte">Joseph</a>, and younger siblings: <a href="/wiki/Lucien_Bonaparte" title="Lucien Bonaparte">Lucien</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elisa_Bonaparte" title="Elisa Bonaparte">Elisa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Louis_Bonaparte" title="Louis Bonaparte">Louis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pauline_Bonaparte" title="Pauline Bonaparte">Pauline</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Bonaparte" title="Caroline Bonaparte">Caroline</a>, and <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A9r%C3%B4me_Bonaparte" title="Jérôme Bonaparte">Jérôme</a>. A boy and girl were born before Joseph but died in infancy. Napoleon was baptised as a Catholic.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>Napoleon's noble, moderately affluent background afforded him greater opportunities to study than were available to a typical Corsican of the time.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[20]</a></sup> In January 1779, he was enrolled at a religious school in <a href="/wiki/Autun" title="Autun">Autun</a>. In May, he was admitted to a <a href="/wiki/Military_academy" title="Military academy">military academy</a> at <a href="/wiki/Brienne-le-Ch%C3%A2teau" title="Brienne-le-Château">Brienne-le-Château</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rxvi_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rxvi-23">[21]</a></sup> His first language was <a href="/wiki/Corsican_language" title="Corsican language">Corsican</a>, and he always spoke French with a marked Corsican accent and never learned to spell French properly.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[22]</a></sup> He was teased by other students for his accent and applied himself to reading.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[23]</a></sup> An examiner observed that Napoleon "has always been distinguished for his application in mathematics. He is fairly well acquainted with history and geography... This boy would make an excellent sailor".<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[note 3]</a></sup></p>
<p>On completion of his studies at Brienne in 1784, Napoleon was admitted to the elite <i><a href="/wiki/%C3%89cole_Militaire" title="École Militaire">École Militaire</a></i> in Paris. He trained to become an artillery officer and, when his father's death reduced his income, was forced to complete the two-year course in one year.<sup id="cite_ref-dwyer42_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dwyer42-29">[26]</a></sup> He was the first Corsican to graduate from the École Militaire.<sup id="cite_ref-dwyer42_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dwyer42-29">[26]</a></sup> He was examined by the famed scientist <a href="/wiki/Pierre-Simon_Laplace" title="Pierre-Simon Laplace">Pierre-Simon Laplace</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[27]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career">Early career</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Napoleon_-_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Napoleon_-_2.jpg/170px-Napoleon_-_2.jpg" width="170" height="243" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Napoleon_-_2.jpg/255px-Napoleon_-_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Napoleon_-_2.jpg/340px-Napoleon_-_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="841" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Napoleon_-_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Napoleon Bonaparte, aged 23, lieutenant-colonel of a battalion of Corsican <a href="/wiki/National_Guard_(France)" title="National Guard (France)">Republican volunteers</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Upon graduating in September 1785, Bonaparte was <a href="/wiki/Officer_(armed_forces)" title="Officer (armed forces)">commissioned</a> a <a href="/wiki/Second_lieutenant" title="Second lieutenant">second lieutenant</a> in <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9giment_de_La_F%C3%A8re_(1765)" class="mw-redirect" title="Régiment de La Fère (1765)"><i>La Fère</i> artillery regiment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rxvi_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rxvi-23">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[note 4]</a></sup> He served in <a href="/wiki/Valence,_Dr%C3%B4me" title="Valence, Drôme">Valence</a> and <a href="/wiki/Auxonne" title="Auxonne">Auxonne</a> until after the outbreak of the Revolution in 1789, and took nearly two years' leave in Corsica and Paris during this period. At this time, he was a fervent <a href="/wiki/Corsican_nationalist" class="mw-redirect" title="Corsican nationalist">Corsican nationalist</a>, and wrote to Corsican leader <a href="/wiki/Pasquale_Paoli" title="Pasquale Paoli">Pasquale Paoli</a> in May 1789, "As the nation was perishing I was born. Thirty thousand Frenchmen were vomited on to our shores, drowning the throne of liberty in waves of blood. Such was the odious sight which was the first to strike me".<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>He spent the early years of the Revolution in Corsica, fighting in a complex three-way struggle among royalists, revolutionaries, and Corsican nationalists. He was a supporter of the republican <a href="/wiki/Jacobin" title="Jacobin">Jacobin</a> movement, organising clubs in Corsica,<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[30]</a></sup> and was given command over a battalion of volunteers. He was promoted to captain in the regular army in July 1792, despite exceeding his leave of absence and leading a riot against French troops.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>He came into conflict with Paoli, who had decided to split with France and sabotage the French assault on the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sardinia" title="Kingdom of Sardinia">Sardinian</a> island of <a href="/wiki/La_Maddalena" title="La Maddalena">La Maddalena</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[32]</a></sup> Bonaparte and his family fled to the French mainland in June 1793 because of the split with Paoli.<sup id="cite_ref-rxviii_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rxviii-37">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Siege_of_Toulon">Siege of Toulon</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Toulon" title="Siege of Toulon">Siege of Toulon</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Napoleon_%C3%A0_Toulon_par_Edouard_Detaille.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Napoleon_%C3%A0_Toulon_par_Edouard_Detaille.jpg/170px-Napoleon_%C3%A0_Toulon_par_Edouard_Detaille.jpg" width="170" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Napoleon_%C3%A0_Toulon_par_Edouard_Detaille.jpg/255px-Napoleon_%C3%A0_Toulon_par_Edouard_Detaille.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Napoleon_%C3%A0_Toulon_par_Edouard_Detaille.jpg/340px-Napoleon_%C3%A0_Toulon_par_Edouard_Detaille.jpg 2x" data-file-width="795" data-file-height="1024" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Napoleon_%C3%A0_Toulon_par_Edouard_Detaille.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bonaparte at the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Toulon" title="Siege of Toulon">Siege of Toulon</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In July 1793, Bonaparte published a pro-republican pamphlet entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Le_souper_de_Beaucaire" title="Le souper de Beaucaire">Le souper de Beaucaire</a></i> (Supper at <a href="/wiki/Beaucaire,_Gard" title="Beaucaire, Gard">Beaucaire</a>) which gained him the support of <a href="/wiki/Augustin_Robespierre" title="Augustin Robespierre">Augustin Robespierre</a>, younger brother of the Revolutionary leader <a href="/wiki/Maximilien_Robespierre" title="Maximilien Robespierre">Maximilien Robespierre</a>. With the help of his fellow Corsican <a href="/wiki/Antoine_Christophe_Saliceti" title="Antoine Christophe Saliceti">Antoine Christophe Saliceti</a>, Bonaparte was appointed artillery commander of the republican forces at the Siege of Toulon.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>He adopted a plan to capture a hill where republican guns could dominate the city's harbour and force the British to evacuate. The assault on the position led to the capture of the city, but during it Bonaparte was wounded in the thigh. He was promoted to <a href="/wiki/Brigadier_general_(France)" class="mw-redirect" title="Brigadier general (France)">brigadier general</a> at the age of 24. Catching the attention of the <a href="/wiki/Committee_of_Public_Safety" title="Committee of Public Safety">Committee of Public Safety</a>, he was put in charge of the artillery of France's <a href="/wiki/Army_of_Italy_(France)" title="Army of Italy (France)">Army of Italy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Napoleon spent time as inspector of coastal fortifications on the Mediterranean coast near <a href="/wiki/Marseille" title="Marseille">Marseille</a> while he was waiting for confirmation of the Army of Italy post. He devised plans for attacking the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sardinia" title="Kingdom of Sardinia">Kingdom of Sardinia</a> as part of France's campaign <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_First_Coalition" title="War of the First Coalition">against the First Coalition</a>. Augustin Robespierre and Saliceti were ready to listen to the freshly promoted artillery general.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>The French army carried out Bonaparte's plan in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Saorgio" title="Battle of Saorgio">Battle of Saorgio</a> in April 1794, and then advanced to seize <a href="/wiki/Ormea" title="Ormea">Ormea</a> in the mountains. From Ormea, they headed west to outflank the Austro-Sardinian positions around <a href="/wiki/Saorge" title="Saorge">Saorge</a>. After this campaign, Augustin Robespierre sent Bonaparte on a mission to the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Republic of Genoa</a> to determine that country's intentions towards France.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="13_Vendémiaire"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="13_Vend.C3.A9miaire">13 Vendémiaire</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/13_Vend%C3%A9miaire" title="13 Vendémiaire">13 Vendémiaire</a></div>
<p>Some contemporaries alleged that Bonaparte was put under <a href="/wiki/House_arrest" title="House arrest">house arrest</a> at <a href="/wiki/Nice" title="Nice">Nice</a> for his association with the Robespierres following their fall in the <a href="/wiki/Thermidorian_Reaction" title="Thermidorian Reaction">Thermidorian Reaction</a> in July 1794, but Napoleon's secretary <a href="/wiki/Louis_Antoine_Fauvelet_de_Bourrienne" title="Louis Antoine Fauvelet de Bourrienne">Bourrienne</a> disputed the allegation in his memoirs. According to Bourrienne, jealousy was responsible, between the Army of the Alps and the Army of Italy (with whom Napoleon was seconded at the time).<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[38]</a></sup> Bonaparte dispatched an impassioned defense in a letter to the commissar Saliceti, and he was subsequently acquitted of any wrongdoing.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>He was released within two weeks and, due to his technical skills, was asked to draw up plans to attack Italian positions in the context of France's war with Austria. He also took part in an expedition to take back Corsica from the British, but the French were repulsed by the British Royal Navy.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>By 1795, Bonaparte had become engaged to <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9sir%C3%A9e_Clary" title="Désirée Clary">Désirée Clary</a>, daughter of <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Clary" title="François Clary">François Clary</a>. Désirée's sister <a href="/wiki/Julie_Clary" title="Julie Clary">Julie Clary</a> had married Bonaparte's elder brother Joseph.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[41]</a></sup> In April 1795, he was assigned to the <a href="/wiki/Army_of_the_West_(1793)" title="Army of the West (1793)">Army of the West</a>, which was engaged in the <a href="/wiki/War_in_the_Vend%C3%A9e" title="War in the Vendée">War in the Vendée</a>—a civil war and royalist <a href="/wiki/Counter-revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="Counter-revolution">counter-revolution</a> in Vendée, a region in west central France on the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>. As an infantry command, it was a demotion from artillery general—for which the army already had a full quota—and he pleaded poor health to avoid the posting.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[42]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:13Vend%C3%A9miaire.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Etching of a street, there are a lot pockets of smoke due to a group of republican artillery firing on royalists across the street at the entrance to a building" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/13Vend%C3%A9miaire.jpg/220px-13Vend%C3%A9miaire.jpg" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/13Vend%C3%A9miaire.jpg/330px-13Vend%C3%A9miaire.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/13Vend%C3%A9miaire.jpg/440px-13Vend%C3%A9miaire.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1418" data-file-height="875" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:13Vend%C3%A9miaire.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Journée du <a href="/wiki/13_Vend%C3%A9miaire" title="13 Vendémiaire">13 Vendémiaire</a></i>. Artillery fire in front of the <i><a href="/wiki/Church_of_Saint-Roch,_Paris" class="mw-redirect" title="Church of Saint-Roch, Paris">Church of Saint-Roch, Paris</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Rue_Saint-Honor%C3%A9" title="Rue Saint-Honoré">Rue Saint-Honoré</a></i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>He was moved to the Bureau of <a href="/wiki/Topography" title="Topography">Topography</a> of the Committee of Public Safety and sought unsuccessfully to be transferred to <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> in order to offer his services to the <a href="/wiki/Sultan" title="Sultan">Sultan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[43]</a></sup> During this period, he wrote the romantic novella <i><a href="/wiki/Clisson_et_Eug%C3%A9nie" title="Clisson et Eugénie">Clisson et Eugénie</a></i>, about a soldier and his lover, in a clear parallel to Bonaparte's own relationship with Désirée.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[44]</a></sup> On 15 September, Bonaparte was removed from the list of generals in regular service for his refusal to serve in the Vendée campaign. He faced a difficult financial situation and reduced career prospects.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 3 October, royalists in Paris declared a rebellion against the <a href="/wiki/National_Convention" title="National Convention">National Convention</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-m96_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-m96-50">[46]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Paul_Fran%C3%A7ois_Jean_Nicolas,_vicomte_de_Barras" class="mw-redirect" title="Paul François Jean Nicolas, vicomte de Barras">Paul Barras</a>, a leader of the Thermidorian Reaction, knew of Bonaparte's military exploits at Toulon and gave him command of the improvised forces in defence of the Convention in the <a href="/wiki/Tuileries_Palace" title="Tuileries Palace">Tuileries Palace</a>. Napoleon had seen the <a href="/wiki/10_August_(French_Revolution)#Assault_on_the_Tuileries" title="10 August (French Revolution)">massacre of the King's Swiss Guard</a> there three years earlier and realised that artillery would be the key to its defence.<sup id="cite_ref-rxvi_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rxvi-23">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>He ordered a young cavalry officer named <a href="/wiki/Joachim_Murat" title="Joachim Murat">Joachim Murat</a> to seize large <a href="/wiki/Cannon" title="Cannon">cannons</a> and used them to repel the attackers on 5 October 1795—<i>13 Vendémiaire An IV</i> in the <a href="/wiki/French_Republican_Calendar" title="French Republican Calendar">French Republican Calendar</a>. 1,400 royalists died and the rest fled.<sup id="cite_ref-m96_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-m96-50">[46]</a></sup> He had cleared the streets with "a whiff of <a href="/wiki/Grapeshot" title="Grapeshot">grapeshot</a>", according to 19th-century historian <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Carlyle" title="Thomas Carlyle">Thomas Carlyle</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_French_Revolution:_A_History" title="The French Revolution: A History">The French Revolution: A History</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>The defeat of the royalist insurrection extinguished the threat to the Convention and earned Bonaparte sudden fame, wealth, and the patronage of the new government, the <a href="/wiki/French_Directory" title="French Directory">Directory</a>. Murat married one of Napoleon's sisters and became his brother-in-law; he also served under Napoleon as one of his generals. Bonaparte was promoted to Commander of the Interior and given command of the Army of Italy.<sup id="cite_ref-rxviii_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rxviii-37">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>Within weeks, he was romantically attached to <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9phine_de_Beauharnais" title="Joséphine de Beauharnais">Joséphine de Beauharnais</a>, the former mistress of Barras. The couple married on 9 March 1796 in a civil ceremony.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_Italian_campaign">First Italian campaign</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Italian_campaigns_of_the_French_Revolutionary_Wars" title="Italian campaigns of the French Revolutionary Wars">Italian campaigns of the French Revolutionary Wars</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1801_Antoine-Jean_Gros_-_Bonaparte_on_the_Bridge_at_Arcole.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A three-quarter-length depiction of Bonaparte, with black tunic and leather gloves, holding a standard and sword, turning backwards to look at his troops" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/1801_Antoine-Jean_Gros_-_Bonaparte_on_the_Bridge_at_Arcole.jpg/170px-1801_Antoine-Jean_Gros_-_Bonaparte_on_the_Bridge_at_Arcole.jpg" width="170" height="240" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/1801_Antoine-Jean_Gros_-_Bonaparte_on_the_Bridge_at_Arcole.jpg/255px-1801_Antoine-Jean_Gros_-_Bonaparte_on_the_Bridge_at_Arcole.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/1801_Antoine-Jean_Gros_-_Bonaparte_on_the_Bridge_at_Arcole.jpg/340px-1801_Antoine-Jean_Gros_-_Bonaparte_on_the_Bridge_at_Arcole.jpg 2x" data-file-width="990" data-file-height="1400" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1801_Antoine-Jean_Gros_-_Bonaparte_on_the_Bridge_at_Arcole.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i><a href="/wiki/Bonaparte_at_the_Pont_d%27Arcole" title="Bonaparte at the Pont d'Arcole">Bonaparte at the Pont d'Arcole</a></i>, by Baron <a href="/wiki/Antoine-Jean_Gros" title="Antoine-Jean Gros">Antoine-Jean Gros</a>, (<a href="/wiki/Circa" title="Circa">ca.</a> 1801), <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_du_Louvre" class="mw-redirect" title="Musée du Louvre">Musée du Louvre</a>, Paris</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Two days after the marriage, Bonaparte left Paris to take command of the Army of Italy. He immediately went on the offensive, hoping to defeat the forces of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sardinia" title="Kingdom of Sardinia">Piedmont</a> before their Austrian allies could intervene. In a series of rapid victories during the <a href="/wiki/Montenotte_Campaign" title="Montenotte Campaign">Montenotte Campaign</a>, he knocked Piedmont out of the war in two weeks. The French then focused on the Austrians for the remainder of the war, the highlight of which became the protracted <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Mantua_(1796%E2%80%9397)" title="Siege of Mantua (1796–97)">struggle for Mantua</a>. The Austrians launched a series of offensives against the French to break the siege, but Napoleon defeated every relief effort, scoring victories at the battles of <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Castiglione" title="Battle of Castiglione">Castiglione</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Bassano" title="Battle of Bassano">Bassano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Arcole" title="Battle of Arcole">Arcole</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Rivoli" title="Battle of Rivoli">Rivoli</a>. The decisive French triumph at Rivoli in January 1797 led to the collapse of the Austrian position in Italy. At Rivoli, the Austrians lost up to 14,000 men while the French lost about 5,000.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBell201529_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBell201529-54">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>The next phase of the campaign featured the French invasion of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">Habsburg</a> heartlands. French forces in Southern Germany had been defeated by the <a href="/wiki/Archduke_Charles,_Duke_of_Teschen" title="Archduke Charles, Duke of Teschen">Archduke Charles</a> in 1796, but the Archduke withdrew his forces to protect Vienna after learning about Napoleon's assault. In the first encounter between the two commanders, Napoleon pushed back his opponent and advanced deep into Austrian territory after winning at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tarvis_(1797)" title="Battle of Tarvis (1797)">Battle of Tarvis</a> in March 1797. The Austrians were alarmed by the French thrust that reached all the way to <a href="/wiki/Leoben" title="Leoben">Leoben</a>, about 100&#160;km from Vienna, and finally decided to sue for peace.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[51]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Leoben" title="Treaty of Leoben">Treaty of Leoben</a>, followed by the more comprehensive <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Campo_Formio" title="Treaty of Campo Formio">Treaty of Campo Formio</a>, gave France control of most of northern Italy and the <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries" title="Low Countries">Low Countries</a>, and a secret clause promised the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">Republic of Venice</a> to Austria. Bonaparte marched on Venice and forced its surrender, ending 1,100 years of independence. He also authorized the French to loot treasures such as the <a href="/wiki/Horses_of_Saint_Mark" title="Horses of Saint Mark">Horses of Saint Mark</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>His application of conventional military ideas to real-world situations enabled his military triumphs, such as creative use of artillery as a mobile force to support his infantry. He stated later in life:<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (August 2016)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> "I have fought sixty battles and I have learned nothing which I did not know at the beginning. Look at Caesar; he fought the first like the last".<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bonaparte could win battles by concealment of troop deployments and concentration of his forces on the "hinge" of an enemy's weakened front. If he could not use his favourite <a href="/wiki/Pincer_movement" title="Pincer movement">envelopment strategy</a>, he would take up the central position and attack two co-operating forces at their hinge, swing round to fight one until it fled, then turn to face the other.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[54]</a></sup> In this Italian campaign, Bonaparte's army captured 150,000 prisoners, 540 cannons, and 170 <a href="/wiki/Flag" title="Flag">standards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[55]</a></sup> The French army fought 67 actions and won 18 <a href="/wiki/Pitched_battle" title="Pitched battle">pitched battles</a> through superior artillery technology and Bonaparte's tactics.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the campaign, Bonaparte became increasingly influential in French politics. He founded two newspapers: one for the troops in his army and another for circulation in France.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[57]</a></sup> The royalists attacked Bonaparte for looting Italy and warned that he might become a dictator.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[58]</a></sup> All told, Napoleon's forces extracted an estimated $45 million in funds from Italy during their campaign there, another $12 million in precious metals and jewels; atop that, his forces confiscated more than three-hundred priceless paintings and sculptures.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBell201530_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBell201530-63">[59]</a></sup> Bonaparte sent General <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Augereau" title="Pierre Augereau">Pierre Augereau</a> to Paris to lead a <i>coup d'état</i> and purge the royalists on 4 September—<a href="/wiki/Coup_of_18_Fructidor" title="Coup of 18 Fructidor">Coup of 18 Fructidor</a>. This left Barras and his Republican allies in control again but dependent on Bonaparte, who proceeded to peace negotiations with Austria. These negotiations resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Campo_Formio" title="Treaty of Campo Formio">Treaty of Campo Formio</a>, and Bonaparte returned to Paris in December as a hero.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[60]</a></sup> He met <a href="/wiki/Charles_Maurice_de_Talleyrand-P%C3%A9rigord" title="Charles Maurice de Talleyrand-Périgord">Talleyrand</a>, France's new Foreign Minister—who served in the same capacity for Emperor Napoleon—and they began to prepare for an invasion of Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-rxviii_37-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rxviii-37">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Egyptian_expedition">Egyptian expedition</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/French_campaign_in_Egypt_and_Syria" title="French campaign in Egypt and Syria">French campaign in Egypt and Syria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jean-L%C3%A9on_G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me_003.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Person on a horse looks towards a giant statue of a head in the desert, with a blue sky" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Jean-L%C3%A9on_G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me_003.jpg/220px-Jean-L%C3%A9on_G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me_003.jpg" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Jean-L%C3%A9on_G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me_003.jpg/330px-Jean-L%C3%A9on_G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me_003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Jean-L%C3%A9on_G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me_003.jpg/440px-Jean-L%C3%A9on_G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me_003.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3071" data-file-height="1838" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jean-L%C3%A9on_G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me_003.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i><a href="/wiki/Bonaparte_Before_the_Sphinx" title="Bonaparte Before the Sphinx">Bonaparte Before the Sphinx</a></i>, (ca. 1868) by <a href="/wiki/Jean-L%C3%A9on_G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me" title="Jean-Léon Gérôme">Jean-Léon Gérôme</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hearst_Castle" title="Hearst Castle">Hearst Castle</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Louis-Fran%C3%A7ois_Baron_Lejeune_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Cavalry battlescene with pyramids in background" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Louis-Fran%C3%A7ois_Baron_Lejeune_001.jpg/220px-Louis-Fran%C3%A7ois_Baron_Lejeune_001.jpg" width="220" height="95" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Louis-Fran%C3%A7ois_Baron_Lejeune_001.jpg/330px-Louis-Fran%C3%A7ois_Baron_Lejeune_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Louis-Fran%C3%A7ois_Baron_Lejeune_001.jpg/440px-Louis-Fran%C3%A7ois_Baron_Lejeune_001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1298" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Louis-Fran%C3%A7ois_Baron_Lejeune_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Battle of the Pyramids</i> on 21 July 1798 by <a href="/wiki/Louis-Fran%C3%A7ois,_Baron_Lejeune" class="mw-redirect" title="Louis-François, Baron Lejeune">Louis-François, Baron Lejeune</a>, 1808</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After two months of planning, Bonaparte decided that France's naval power was not yet strong enough to confront the British Royal Navy. He decided on a military expedition to seize Egypt and thereby undermine Britain's access to its <a href="/wiki/Company_rule_in_India#Trade" title="Company rule in India">trade interests in India</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rxviii_37-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rxviii-37">[33]</a></sup> Bonaparte wished to establish a French presence in the Middle East, with the ultimate dream of linking with <a href="/wiki/Tipu_Sultan" title="Tipu Sultan">Tipu Sultan</a>, a Muslim enemy of the British in India.<sup id="cite_ref-Watson_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Watson-65">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>Napoleon assured the Directory that "as soon as he had conquered Egypt, he will establish relations with the Indian princes and, together with them, attack the English in their possessions".<sup id="cite_ref-Amini_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amini-66">[62]</a></sup> The Directory agreed in order to secure a trade route to India.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 1798, Bonaparte was elected a member of the <a href="/wiki/French_Academy_of_Sciences" title="French Academy of Sciences">French Academy of Sciences</a>. His Egyptian expedition included a group of 167 scientists, with mathematicians, naturalists, chemists, and <a href="/wiki/Geodesy" title="Geodesy">geodesists</a> among them. Their discoveries included the <a href="/wiki/Rosetta_Stone" title="Rosetta Stone">Rosetta Stone</a>, and their work was published in the <i><a href="/wiki/Description_de_l%27%C3%89gypte" title="Description de l'Égypte">Description de l'Égypte</a></i> in 1809.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>En route to Egypt, Bonaparte reached <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a> on 9 June 1798, then controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Knights_Hospitaller" title="Knights Hospitaller">Knights Hospitaller</a>. Grand Master <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_von_Hompesch_zu_Bolheim" title="Ferdinand von Hompesch zu Bolheim">Ferdinand von Hompesch zu Bolheim</a> surrendered after token resistance, and Bonaparte captured an important naval base with the loss of only three men.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>General Bonaparte and his expedition eluded pursuit by the Royal Navy and landed at <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">Alexandria</a> on 1 July.<sup id="cite_ref-rxviii_37-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rxviii-37">[33]</a></sup> He fought the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Shubra_Khit" title="Battle of Shubra Khit">Battle of Shubra Khit</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Mamluk" title="Mamluk">Mamluks</a>, Egypt's ruling military caste. This helped the French practice their defensive tactic for the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Pyramids" title="Battle of the Pyramids">Battle of the Pyramids</a>, fought on 21 July, about 24&#160;km (15&#160;mi) from the <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_pyramids" title="Egyptian pyramids">pyramids</a>. General Bonaparte's forces of 25,000 roughly equalled those of the Mamluks' Egyptian cavalry. Twenty-nine French<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[66]</a></sup> and approximately 2,000 Egyptians were killed. The victory boosted the morale of the French army.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 1 August 1798, the British fleet under <a href="/wiki/Horatio_Nelson" class="mw-redirect" title="Horatio Nelson">Horatio Nelson</a> captured or destroyed all but two French vessels in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Nile" title="Battle of the Nile">Battle of the Nile</a>, defeating Bonaparte's goal to strengthen the French position in the Mediterranean.<sup id="cite_ref-rxx_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rxx-72">[68]</a></sup> His army had succeeded in a temporary increase of French power in Egypt, though it faced repeated uprisings.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[69]</a></sup> In early 1799, he moved an army into the <a href="/wiki/Wilayah" title="Wilayah">Ottoman province</a> of Damascus (Syria and <a href="/wiki/Galilee" title="Galilee">Galilee</a>). Bonaparte led these 13,000 French soldiers in the conquest of the coastal towns of <a href="/wiki/Arish" title="Arish">Arish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gaza_City" title="Gaza City">Gaza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jaffa" title="Jaffa">Jaffa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Haifa" title="Haifa">Haifa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[70]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Jaffa" title="Siege of Jaffa">attack on Jaffa</a> was particularly brutal. Bonaparte discovered that many of the defenders were former prisoners of war, ostensibly on <a href="/wiki/Prisoners_of_war_parole" class="mw-redirect" title="Prisoners of war parole">parole</a>, so he ordered the garrison and 1,400 prisoners to be executed by bayonet or drowning to save bullets.<sup id="cite_ref-rxx_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rxx-72">[68]</a></sup> Men, women, and children were robbed and murdered for three days.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bonaparte began with an army of 13,000 men; 1,500 were reported missing, 1,200 died in combat, and thousands perished from disease—mostly <a href="/wiki/Bubonic_plague" title="Bubonic plague">bubonic plague</a>. He failed to <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Acre_(1799)" title="Siege of Acre (1799)">reduce the fortress</a> of <a href="/wiki/Acre,_Israel" title="Acre, Israel">Acre</a>, so he marched his army back to Egypt in May. To speed up the retreat, Bonaparte ordered plague-stricken men to be poisoned with opium; the number who died remains disputed, ranging from a low of 30 to a high of 580. He also brought out 1,000 wounded men.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[72]</a></sup> Back in Egypt on 25 July, Bonaparte defeated an <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Abukir_(1799)" title="Battle of Abukir (1799)">Ottoman amphibious invasion at Abukir</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[73]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ruler_of_France">Ruler of France</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Coup_of_18_Brumaire" title="Coup of 18 Brumaire">18 Brumaire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_era" title="Napoleonic era">Napoleonic era</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bouchot_-_Le_general_Bonaparte_au_Conseil_des_Cinq-Cents.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Bonaparte in a simple general uniform in the middle of a scrum of red-robbed members of the Council of Five Hundred" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Bouchot_-_Le_general_Bonaparte_au_Conseil_des_Cinq-Cents.jpg/220px-Bouchot_-_Le_general_Bonaparte_au_Conseil_des_Cinq-Cents.jpg" width="220" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Bouchot_-_Le_general_Bonaparte_au_Conseil_des_Cinq-Cents.jpg/330px-Bouchot_-_Le_general_Bonaparte_au_Conseil_des_Cinq-Cents.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Bouchot_-_Le_general_Bonaparte_au_Conseil_des_Cinq-Cents.jpg/440px-Bouchot_-_Le_general_Bonaparte_au_Conseil_des_Cinq-Cents.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1305" data-file-height="1400" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bouchot_-_Le_general_Bonaparte_au_Conseil_des_Cinq-Cents.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
General Bonaparte surrounded by members of the Council of Five Hundred during the Coup of 18 Brumaire, by <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Bouchot" title="François Bouchot">François Bouchot</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>While in Egypt, Bonaparte stayed informed of European affairs. He learned that France had suffered a <a href="/wiki/Campaigns_of_1799_in_the_French_Revolutionary_Wars" title="Campaigns of 1799 in the French Revolutionary Wars">series of defeats</a> in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Second_Coalition" title="War of the Second Coalition">War of the Second Coalition</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-egyptreturn_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-egyptreturn-78">[74]</a></sup> On 24 August 1799, he took advantage of the temporary departure of British ships from French coastal ports and set sail for France, despite the fact that he had received no explicit orders from Paris.<sup id="cite_ref-rxx_72-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rxx-72">[68]</a></sup> The army was left in the charge of <a href="/wiki/Jean_Baptiste_Kl%C3%A9ber" class="mw-redirect" title="Jean Baptiste Kléber">Jean Baptiste Kléber</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>Unknown to Bonaparte, the Directory had sent him orders to return to ward off possible invasions of French soil, but poor lines of communication prevented the delivery of these messages.<sup id="cite_ref-egyptreturn_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-egyptreturn-78">[74]</a></sup> By the time that he reached Paris in October, France's situation had been improved by a series of victories. The Republic, however, was bankrupt and the ineffective Directory was unpopular with the French population.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[76]</a></sup> The Directory discussed Bonaparte's "desertion" but was too weak to punish him.<sup id="cite_ref-egyptreturn_78-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-egyptreturn-78">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite the failures in Egypt, Napoleon returned to a hero's welcome. He drew together an alliance with director <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Joseph_Siey%C3%A8s" title="Emmanuel Joseph Sieyès">Emmanuel Joseph Sieyès</a>, his brother Lucien, speaker of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Five_Hundred" title="Council of Five Hundred">Council of Five Hundred</a> <a href="/wiki/Roger_Ducos" title="Roger Ducos">Roger Ducos</a>, director <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Fouch%C3%A9" title="Joseph Fouché">Joseph Fouché</a>, and Talleyrand, and they overthrew the Directory by a <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">coup d'état</a> on 9 November 1799 ("the 18th Brumaire" according to the revolutionary calendar), closing down the council of five hundred. Napoleon became "first consul" for ten years, with two consuls appointed by him who had consultative voices only. His power was confirmed by the new "<a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Year_VIII" title="Constitution of the Year VIII">Constitution of the Year VIII</a>", originally devised by Sieyès to give Napoleon a minor role, but rewritten by Napoleon, and accepted by direct popular vote (3,000,000 in favor, 1,567 opposed). The constitution preserved the appearance of a republic but in reality established a dictatorship.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French_Consulate">French Consulate</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/French_Consulate" title="French Consulate">French Consulate</a> and <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Second_Coalition" title="War of the Second Coalition">War of the Second Coalition</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jean_Auguste_Dominique_Ingres,_Portrait_de_Napol%C3%A9on_Bonaparte_en_premier_consul.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Jean_Auguste_Dominique_Ingres%2C_Portrait_de_Napol%C3%A9on_Bonaparte_en_premier_consul.jpg/170px-Jean_Auguste_Dominique_Ingres%2C_Portrait_de_Napol%C3%A9on_Bonaparte_en_premier_consul.jpg" width="170" height="264" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Jean_Auguste_Dominique_Ingres%2C_Portrait_de_Napol%C3%A9on_Bonaparte_en_premier_consul.jpg/255px-Jean_Auguste_Dominique_Ingres%2C_Portrait_de_Napol%C3%A9on_Bonaparte_en_premier_consul.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Jean_Auguste_Dominique_Ingres%2C_Portrait_de_Napol%C3%A9on_Bonaparte_en_premier_consul.jpg/340px-Jean_Auguste_Dominique_Ingres%2C_Portrait_de_Napol%C3%A9on_Bonaparte_en_premier_consul.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1860" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jean_Auguste_Dominique_Ingres,_Portrait_de_Napol%C3%A9on_Bonaparte_en_premier_consul.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i><a href="/wiki/Bonaparte,_First_Consul" title="Bonaparte, First Consul">Bonaparte, First Consul</a></i>, by <a href="/wiki/Jean_Auguste_Dominique_Ingres" class="mw-redirect" title="Jean Auguste Dominique Ingres">Ingres</a>. Posing <a href="/wiki/Hand-in-waistcoat" title="Hand-in-waistcoat">the hand inside the waistcoat</a> was often used in portraits of rulers to indicate calm and stable leadership.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_liitle_grey_coated_figure_of_the_soldiers_Hero.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/The_liitle_grey_coated_figure_of_the_soldiers_Hero.jpg/220px-The_liitle_grey_coated_figure_of_the_soldiers_Hero.jpg" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/The_liitle_grey_coated_figure_of_the_soldiers_Hero.jpg/330px-The_liitle_grey_coated_figure_of_the_soldiers_Hero.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/The_liitle_grey_coated_figure_of_the_soldiers_Hero.jpg/440px-The_liitle_grey_coated_figure_of_the_soldiers_Hero.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1550" data-file-height="2328" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_liitle_grey_coated_figure_of_the_soldiers_Hero.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Napoleon as commander of the Army</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Napoleon established a political system that historian <a href="/wiki/Martyn_Lyons" title="Martyn Lyons">Martyn Lyons</a> called "dictatorship by plebiscite".<sup id="cite_ref-Lyons.2C_Martyn_1994.2C_p._111_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lyons.2C_Martyn_1994.2C_p._111-83">[79]</a></sup> Worried by the democratic forces unleashed by the Revolution, but unwilling to ignore them entirely, Napoleon resorted to regular electoral consultations with the French people on his road to imperial power.<sup id="cite_ref-Lyons.2C_Martyn_1994.2C_p._111_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lyons.2C_Martyn_1994.2C_p._111-83">[79]</a></sup> He drafted the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Year_VIII" title="Constitution of the Year VIII">Constitution of the Year VIII</a> and secured his own election as <a href="/wiki/First_Consul" class="mw-redirect" title="First Consul">First Consul</a>, taking up residence at the Tuileries. The constitution was approved in <a href="/wiki/French_constitutional_referendum,_1800" title="French constitutional referendum, 1800">a rigged plebiscite</a> held the following January, with 99.94 percent officially listed as voting "yes".<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[80]</a></sup> Napoleon's brother, Lucien, had falsified the returns to show that 3 million people had participated in the plebiscite; the real number was 1.5 million.<sup id="cite_ref-Lyons.2C_Martyn_1994.2C_p._111_83-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lyons.2C_Martyn_1994.2C_p._111-83">[79]</a></sup> Political observers at the time assumed the eligible French voting public numbered about 5 million people, so the regime artificially doubled the participation rate to indicate popular enthusiasm for the Consulate.<sup id="cite_ref-Lyons.2C_Martyn_1994.2C_p._111_83-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lyons.2C_Martyn_1994.2C_p._111-83">[79]</a></sup> In the first few months of the Consulate, with war in Europe still raging and internal instability still plaguing the country, Napoleon's grip on power remained very tenuous.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In the spring of 1800, Napoleon and his troops crossed the Swiss Alps into Italy, aiming to surprise the Austrian armies that had reoccupied the peninsula when Napoleon was still in Egypt.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[note 5]</a></sup> After a difficult crossing over the Alps, the French army entered the plains of Northern Italy virtually unopposed.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[82]</a></sup> While one French army approached from the north, the Austrians were busy with another stationed in <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoa</a>, which was <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Genoa_(1800)" title="Siege of Genoa (1800)">besieged</a> by a substantial force. The fierce resistance of this French army, under <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Mass%C3%A9na" title="André Masséna">André Masséna</a>, gave the northern force some time to carry out their operations with little interference.<sup id="cite_ref-McLynn_1998.2C_p.235_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McLynn_1998.2C_p.235-88">[83]</a></sup> After spending several days looking for each other, the two armies collided at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Marengo" title="Battle of Marengo">Battle of Marengo</a> on 14 June. <a href="/wiki/Michael_von_Melas" title="Michael von Melas">General Melas</a> had a numerical advantage, fielding about 30,000 Austrian soldiers while Napoleon commanded 24,000 French troops.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[84]</a></sup> The battle began favorably for the Austrians as their initial attack surprised the French and gradually drove them back. Melas stated that he'd won the battle and retired to his headquarters around 3 pm, leaving his subordinates in charge of pursuing the French.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[85]</a></sup> The French lines never broke during their tactical retreat; Napoleon constantly rode out among the troops urging them to stand and fight. Late in the afternoon,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (August 2016)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> a full division under <a href="/wiki/Louis_Desaix" title="Louis Desaix">Desaix</a> arrived on the field and reversed the tide of the battle. A series of artillery barrages and cavalry charges decimated the Austrian army, which fled over the <a href="/wiki/Bormida_(river)" title="Bormida (river)">Bormida River</a> back to <a href="/wiki/Alessandria" title="Alessandria">Alessandria</a>, leaving behind 14,000 casualties.<sup id="cite_ref-Chandler.2C_David_1966.2C_p._296_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chandler.2C_David_1966.2C_p._296-91">[86]</a></sup> The following day,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (August 2016)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> the Austrian army agreed to abandon Northern Italy once more with the Convention of Alessandria, which granted them safe passage to friendly soil in exchange for their fortresses throughout the region.<sup id="cite_ref-Chandler.2C_David_1966.2C_p._296_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chandler.2C_David_1966.2C_p._296-91">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although critics have blamed Napoleon for several tactical mistakes preceding the battle, they have also praised his audacity for selecting a risky campaign strategy, choosing to invade the Italian peninsula from the north when the vast majority of French invasions came from the west, near or along the coastline.<sup id="cite_ref-Chandler.2C_David_1966.2C_pp._298-304_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chandler.2C_David_1966.2C_pp._298-304-92">[87]</a></sup> As Chandler points out, Napoleon spent almost a year getting the Austrians out of Italy in his first campaign; in 1800, it took him only a month to achieve the same goal.<sup id="cite_ref-Chandler.2C_David_1966.2C_pp._298-304_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chandler.2C_David_1966.2C_pp._298-304-92">[87]</a></sup> German strategist and field marshal <a href="/wiki/Alfred_von_Schlieffen" title="Alfred von Schlieffen">Alfred von Schlieffen</a> concluded that "Bonaparte did not annihilate his enemy but eliminated him and rendered him harmless" while "[attaining] the object of the campaign: the conquest of North Italy".<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>Napoleon's triumph at Marengo secured his political authority and boosted his popularity back home, but it did not lead to an immediate peace. Bonaparte's brother, Joseph, led the complex negotiations in <a href="/wiki/Lun%C3%A9ville" title="Lunéville">Lunéville</a> and reported that Austria, emboldened by British support, would not acknowledge the new territory that France had acquired. As negotiations became increasingly fractious, Bonaparte gave orders to his general <a href="/wiki/Jean_Victor_Marie_Moreau" title="Jean Victor Marie Moreau">Moreau</a> to strike Austria once more. Moreau and the French swept through <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavaria</a> and scored an overwhelming victory at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hohenlinden" title="Battle of Hohenlinden">Hohenlinden</a> in December 1800. As a result, the Austrians capitulated and signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lun%C3%A9ville" title="Treaty of Lunéville">Treaty of Lunéville</a> in February 1801. The treaty reaffirmed and expanded earlier French gains at <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Campo_Formio" title="Treaty of Campo Formio">Campo Formio</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Schom_1997.2C_p.302_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schom_1997.2C_p.302-94">[89]</a></sup> Britain now remained the only nation that was still at war with France.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Temporary_peace_in_Europe">Temporary peace in Europe</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Revolution" title="Haitian Revolution">Haitian Revolution</a></div>
<p>After a decade of constant warfare, France and Britain signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Amiens" title="Treaty of Amiens">Treaty of Amiens</a> in March 1802, bringing the Revolutionary Wars to an end. Amiens called for the withdrawal of British troops from recently conquered colonial territories as well as for assurances to curtail the expansionary goals of the French Republic.<sup id="cite_ref-McLynn_1998.2C_p.235_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McLynn_1998.2C_p.235-88">[83]</a></sup> With Europe at peace and the economy recovering, Napoleon's popularity soared to its highest levels under the Consulate, both domestically and abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-Lyons.2C_Martyn_1994.2C_pp._111-4_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lyons.2C_Martyn_1994.2C_pp._111-4-95">[90]</a></sup> In a <a href="/wiki/French_constitutional_referendum,_1802" title="French constitutional referendum, 1802">new plebiscite</a> during the spring of 1802, the French public came out in huge numbers to approve a constitution that made the Consulate permanent, essentially elevating Napoleon to dictator for life.<sup id="cite_ref-Lyons.2C_Martyn_1994.2C_pp._111-4_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lyons.2C_Martyn_1994.2C_pp._111-4-95">[90]</a></sup> Whereas the plebiscite two years earlier had brought out 1.5 million people to the polls, the new referendum enticed 3.6 million to go and vote (72% of all eligible voters).<sup id="cite_ref-Lyons.2C_Martyn_1994.2C_p._113_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lyons.2C_Martyn_1994.2C_p._113-96">[91]</a></sup> There was no secret ballot in 1802 and few people wanted to openly defy the regime; the constitution gained approval with over 99% of the vote.<sup id="cite_ref-Lyons.2C_Martyn_1994.2C_p._113_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lyons.2C_Martyn_1994.2C_p._113-96">[91]</a></sup> His broad powers were spelled out in the new constitution: <i>Article 1. The French people name, and the Senate proclaims Napoleon-Bonaparte First Consul for Life.</i><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[92]</a></sup> After 1802, he was generally referred to as Napoleon rather than Bonaparte.<sup id="cite_ref-m290_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-m290-31">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>The brief peace in Europe allowed Napoleon to focus on the French colonies abroad. <a href="/wiki/Saint-Domingue" title="Saint-Domingue">Saint-Domingue</a> had managed to acquire a high level of political autonomy during the Revolutionary Wars, with <a href="/wiki/Toussaint_Louverture" title="Toussaint Louverture">Toussaint Louverture</a> installing himself as de facto dictator by 1801. Napoleon saw his chance to recuperate the formerly wealthy colony when he signed the Treaty of Amiens. During the Revolution, the National Convention voted to abolish slavery in February 1794. Under the terms of Amiens, however, Napoleon agreed to appease British demands by not abolishing slavery in any colonies where the 1794 decree had never been implemented. The resulting <a href="/wiki/Law_of_20_May_1802" title="Law of 20 May 1802">Law of 20 May</a> never applied to colonies like <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a> or <a href="/wiki/Guyane" class="mw-redirect" title="Guyane">Guyane</a>, even though rogue generals and other officials used the pretext of peace as an opportunity to reinstate slavery in some of these places. The Law of 20 May officially restored the slave trade to the Caribbean colonies, not slavery itself.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[93]</a></sup> Napoleon sent <a href="/wiki/Saint-Domingue_expedition" title="Saint-Domingue expedition">an expedition</a> under <a href="/wiki/Charles_Leclerc" title="Charles Leclerc">General Leclerc</a> designed to reassert control over Sainte-Domingue. Although the French managed to capture Toussaint Louverture, the expedition failed when high rates of disease crippled the French army. In May 1803, the last 8000 French troops left the island and the slaves proclaimed an independent republic that they called <a href="/wiki/Ha%C3%AFti" class="mw-redirect" title="Haïti">Haïti</a> in 1804.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[94]</a></sup> Seeing the failure of his colonial efforts, Napoleon decided in 1803 to <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Purchase" title="Louisiana Purchase">sell</a> the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Territory" title="Louisiana Territory">Louisiana Territory</a> to the United States, instantly doubling the size of the U.S. The selling price in the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Purchase" title="Louisiana Purchase">Louisiana Purchase</a> was less than three cents per acre, a total of $15 million.<sup id="cite_ref-Roberts.2C_Andrew_2014_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roberts.2C_Andrew_2014-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>The peace with Britain proved to be uneasy and controversial.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[96]</a></sup> Britain did not evacuate Malta as promised and protested against Bonaparte's <a href="/wiki/Annexation" title="Annexation">annexation</a> of Piedmont and his <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Mediation" title="Act of Mediation">Act of Mediation</a>, which established a new <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Confederation_(Napoleonic)" class="mw-redirect" title="Swiss Confederation (Napoleonic)">Swiss Confederation</a>. Neither of these territories were covered by Amiens, but they inflamed tensions significantly.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[97]</a></sup> The dispute culminated in a declaration of war by Britain in May 1803; Napoleon responded by reassembling the invasion camp at Boulogne.<sup id="cite_ref-rxx_72-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rxx-72">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French_Empire">French Empire</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/First_French_Empire" title="First French Empire">First French Empire</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jacques-Louis_David,_The_Coronation_of_Napoleon_edit.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Colored painting depicting Napoleon crowning his wife inside of a cathedral" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Jacques-Louis_David%2C_The_Coronation_of_Napoleon_edit.jpg/220px-Jacques-Louis_David%2C_The_Coronation_of_Napoleon_edit.jpg" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Jacques-Louis_David%2C_The_Coronation_of_Napoleon_edit.jpg/330px-Jacques-Louis_David%2C_The_Coronation_of_Napoleon_edit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Jacques-Louis_David%2C_The_Coronation_of_Napoleon_edit.jpg/440px-Jacques-Louis_David%2C_The_Coronation_of_Napoleon_edit.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2200" data-file-height="1375" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Coronation_of_Napoleon_I" title="Coronation of Napoleon I">Coronation of Napoleon I</a> and <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bust_of_Napoleon_I,_1807-1809_CE._Marble,_from_Carrara,_Italy._After_Antoine-Denis_Chaudet._The_Victoria_and_Albert_Museum,_London.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Bust_of_Napoleon_I%2C_1807-1809_CE._Marble%2C_from_Carrara%2C_Italy._After_Antoine-Denis_Chaudet._The_Victoria_and_Albert_Museum%2C_London.jpg/220px-Bust_of_Napoleon_I%2C_1807-1809_CE._Marble%2C_from_Carrara%2C_Italy._After_Antoine-Denis_Chaudet._The_Victoria_and_Albert_Museum%2C_London.jpg" width="220" height="312" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Bust_of_Napoleon_I%2C_1807-1809_CE._Marble%2C_from_Carrara%2C_Italy._After_Antoine-Denis_Chaudet._The_Victoria_and_Albert_Museum%2C_London.jpg/330px-Bust_of_Napoleon_I%2C_1807-1809_CE._Marble%2C_from_Carrara%2C_Italy._After_Antoine-Denis_Chaudet._The_Victoria_and_Albert_Museum%2C_London.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Bust_of_Napoleon_I%2C_1807-1809_CE._Marble%2C_from_Carrara%2C_Italy._After_Antoine-Denis_Chaudet._The_Victoria_and_Albert_Museum%2C_London.jpg/440px-Bust_of_Napoleon_I%2C_1807-1809_CE._Marble%2C_from_Carrara%2C_Italy._After_Antoine-Denis_Chaudet._The_Victoria_and_Albert_Museum%2C_London.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3685" data-file-height="5223" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bust_of_Napoleon_I,_1807-1809_CE._Marble,_from_Carrara,_Italy._After_Antoine-Denis_Chaudet._The_Victoria_and_Albert_Museum,_London.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bust of Napoleon I, 1807–1809. Marble, from <a href="/wiki/Carrara,_Italy" class="mw-redirect" title="Carrara, Italy">Carrara, Italy</a>. After Antoine-Denis Chaudet. <a href="/wiki/The_Victoria_and_Albert_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="The Victoria and Albert Museum">The Victoria and Albert Museum</a>, London</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the Consulate, Napoleon faced several royalist and Jacobin <a href="/wiki/Assassination_Attempts_on_Napoleon_Bonaparte" class="mw-redirect" title="Assassination Attempts on Napoleon Bonaparte">assassination plots</a>, including the <i><a href="/wiki/Conspiration_des_poignards" title="Conspiration des poignards">Conspiration des poignards</a></i> (Dagger plot) in October 1800 and the <a href="/wiki/Plot_of_the_Rue_Saint-Nicaise" class="mw-redirect" title="Plot of the Rue Saint-Nicaise">Plot of the Rue Saint-Nicaise</a> (also known as the <i>Infernal Machine</i>) two months later.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[98]</a></sup> In January 1804, his police uncovered an assassination plot against him that involved Moreau and which was ostensibly sponsored by the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Bourbon" title="House of Bourbon">Bourbon</a> family, the former rulers of France. On the advice of Talleyrand, Napoleon ordered the kidnapping of the <a href="/wiki/Louis_Antoine,_Duke_of_Enghien" title="Louis Antoine, Duke of Enghien">Duke of Enghien</a>, violating the sovereignty of <a href="/wiki/Baden" title="Baden">Baden</a>.
