The Duke was quickly executed after a secret military trial, even though he had not been involved in the plot.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[99]</a></sup> Enghien's execution infuriated royal courts throughout Europe, becoming one of the contributing political factors for the outbreak of the Napoleonic Wars.</p>
<p>To expand his power, Napoleon used these <a href="/wiki/Assassination_Attempts_on_Napoleon_Bonaparte" class="mw-redirect" title="Assassination Attempts on Napoleon Bonaparte">assassination plots</a> to justify the creation of an imperial system based on the Roman model. He believed that a Bourbon restoration would be more difficult if his family's succession was entrenched in the constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-m297_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-m297-105">[100]</a></sup> Launching yet <a href="/wiki/French_constitutional_referendum,_1804" title="French constitutional referendum, 1804">another referendum</a>, Napoleon was elected as <i>Emperor of the French</i> by a tally exceeding 99%.<sup id="cite_ref-Lyons.2C_Martyn_1994.2C_p._113_96-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lyons.2C_Martyn_1994.2C_p._113-96">[91]</a></sup> As with the Life Consulate two years earlier, this referendum produced heavy participation, bringing out almost 3.6 million voters to the polls.<sup id="cite_ref-Lyons.2C_Martyn_1994.2C_p._113_96-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lyons.2C_Martyn_1994.2C_p._113-96">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>A keen observer of Bonaparte’s rise to absolute power, <a href="/wiki/Madame_de_R%C3%A9musat" title="Madame de Rémusat">Madame de Rémusat</a>, explains that "men worn out by the turmoil of the Revolution … looked for the domination of an able ruler" and that "people believed quite sincerely that Bonaparte, whether as consul or emperor, would exert his authority and save [them] from the perils of anarchy.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[101]</a></sup>"</p>
<p>Napoleon's coronation took place on 2 December 1804. Two separate crowns were brought for the ceremony: a golden laurel wreath recalling the Roman Empire and a replica of Charlemagne's crown.<sup id="cite_ref-AndrewRoberts2_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AndrewRoberts2-107">[102]</a></sup> Napoleon entered the ceremony wearing the laurel wreath and kept it on his head throughout the proceedings.<sup id="cite_ref-AndrewRoberts2_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AndrewRoberts2-107">[102]</a></sup> For the official coronation, he raised the Charlemagne crown over his own head in a symbolic gesture, but never placed it on top because he was already wearing the golden wreath.<sup id="cite_ref-AndrewRoberts2_107-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AndrewRoberts2-107">[102]</a></sup> Instead he placed the crown on Josephine's head, the event commemorated in the officially sanctioned painting by <a href="/wiki/Jacques-Louis_David" title="Jacques-Louis David">Jacques-Louis David</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AndrewRoberts2_107-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AndrewRoberts2-107">[102]</a></sup> Napoleon was also crowned <a href="/wiki/King_of_Italy" title="King of Italy">King of Italy</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Crown_of_Lombardy" title="Iron Crown of Lombardy">Iron Crown of Lombardy</a>, at the <a href="/wiki/Milan_Cathedral" title="Milan Cathedral">Cathedral of Milan</a> on 26 May 1805. He created eighteen <i><a href="/wiki/Marshal_of_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Marshal of France">Marshals of the Empire</a></i> from amongst his top generals to secure the allegiance of the army.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="War_of_the_Third_Coalition">War of the Third Coalition</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Third_Coalition" title="War of the Third Coalition">War of the Third Coalition</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ulm_capitulation.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Colored painting depicting Napoleon receiving the surrender of the Austrian generals, with the opposing armies and the city of Ulm in the background" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Ulm_capitulation.jpg/220px-Ulm_capitulation.jpg" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Ulm_capitulation.jpg/330px-Ulm_capitulation.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Ulm_capitulation.jpg/440px-Ulm_capitulation.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1965" data-file-height="1238" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ulm_capitulation.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Napoleon and the <i><a href="/wiki/Grande_Arm%C3%A9e" title="Grande Armée">Grande Armée</a></i> receive the surrender of <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Empire" title="Austrian Empire">Austrian</a> <a href="/wiki/Karl_Mack_von_Leiberich" title="Karl Mack von Leiberich">General Mack</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ulm" title="Battle of Ulm">Battle of Ulm</a> in October 1805. The decisive finale of the <a href="/wiki/Ulm_Campaign" title="Ulm Campaign">Ulm Campaign</a> raised the tally of captured Austrian soldiers to 60,000. With the Austrian army destroyed, <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> would fall to the French in November.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Great Britain had broken the Peace of Amiens by declaring war on France in May 1803.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[103]</a></sup> In December 1804, an Anglo-Swedish agreement became the first step towards the creation of the Third Coalition. By April 1805, Britain had also signed an alliance with Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[104]</a></sup> Austria had been defeated by France twice in recent memory and wanted revenge, so it joined the coalition a few months later.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before the formation of the Third Coalition, Napoleon had assembled an invasion force, the <i>Armée d'Angleterre</i>, around six camps at <a href="/wiki/Boulogne-sur-Mer" title="Boulogne-sur-Mer">Boulogne</a> in Northern France. He intended to use this invasion force to strike at England. They never invaded, but Napoleon's troops received careful and invaluable training for future military operations.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[106]</a></sup> The men at Boulogne formed the core for what Napoleon later called <i><a href="/wiki/La_Grande_Arm%C3%A9e" class="mw-redirect" title="La Grande Armée">La Grande Armée</a></i>. At the start, this French army had about 200,000 men organized into seven <a href="/wiki/Corps" title="Corps">corps</a>, which were large field units that contained 36 to 40 <a href="/wiki/Cannon" title="Cannon">cannons</a> each and were capable of independent action until other corps could come to the rescue.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[107]</a></sup> A single corps properly situated in a strong defensive position could survive at least a day without support, giving the <i>Grande Armée</i> countless strategic and tactical options on every campaign. On top of these forces, Napoleon created a <a href="/wiki/Cavalry" title="Cavalry">cavalry</a> reserve of 22,000 organized into two <a href="/wiki/Cuirassier" title="Cuirassier">cuirassier</a> <a href="/wiki/Division_(military)" title="Division (military)">divisions</a>, four mounted <a href="/wiki/Dragoon" title="Dragoon">dragoon</a> divisions, one division of dismounted dragoons, and one of light cavalry, all supported by 24 <a href="/wiki/Artillery" title="Artillery">artillery</a> pieces.<sup id="cite_ref-Chandler_p._333_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chandler_p._333-113">[108]</a></sup> By 1805, the <i>Grande Armée</i> had grown to a force of 350,000 men,<sup id="cite_ref-Chandler_p._333_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chandler_p._333-113">[108]</a></sup> who were well equipped, well trained, and led by competent officers.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>Napoleon knew that the French fleet could not defeat the Royal Navy in a head-to-head battle, so he planned to lure it away from the English Channel through diversionary tactics.<sup id="cite_ref-McLynn_1998.2C_p.321_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McLynn_1998.2C_p.321-115">[110]</a></sup> The main strategic idea involved the <a href="/wiki/French_Navy" title="French Navy">French Navy</a> escaping from the British blockades of <a href="/wiki/Toulon" title="Toulon">Toulon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brest,_France" title="Brest, France">Brest</a> and threatening to attack the West Indies. In the face of this attack, it was hoped, the British would weaken their defense of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Approaches" title="Western Approaches">Western Approaches</a> by sending ships to the Caribbean, allowing a combined Franco-Spanish fleet to take control of the channel long enough for French armies to cross and <a href="/wiki/Napoleon%27s_planned_invasion_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Napoleon's planned invasion of the United Kingdom">invade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-McLynn_1998.2C_p.321_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McLynn_1998.2C_p.321-115">[110]</a></sup> However, the plan unraveled after the British victory at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cape_Finisterre_(1805)" title="Battle of Cape Finisterre (1805)">Battle of Cape Finisterre</a> in July 1805. French <a href="/wiki/Pierre-Charles_Villeneuve" title="Pierre-Charles Villeneuve">Admiral Villeneuve</a> then retreated to <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz" title="Cádiz">Cádiz</a> instead of linking up with French naval forces at Brest for an attack on the <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p>By August 1805, Napoleon had realized that the strategic situation had changed fundamentally. Facing a potential invasion from his continental enemies, he decided to strike first and turned his army's sights from the English Channel to the <a href="/wiki/Rhine_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhine River">Rhine</a>. His basic objective was to destroy the isolated Austrian armies in Southern Germany before their Russian allies could arrive. On 25 September, after great secrecy and feverish marching, 200,000 French troops began to cross the Rhine on a front of 260&#160;km (160&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[112]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[113]</a></sup> Austrian commander <a href="/wiki/Karl_Mack" class="mw-redirect" title="Karl Mack">Karl Mack</a> had gathered the greater part of the Austrian army at the fortress of <a href="/wiki/Ulm" title="Ulm">Ulm</a> in <a href="/wiki/Swabia" title="Swabia">Swabia</a>. Napoleon swung his forces to the southeast and the Grande Armée performed an elaborate wheeling movement that outflanked the Austrian positions. The <a href="/wiki/Ulm_Campaign" title="Ulm Campaign">Ulm Maneuver</a> completely surprised General Mack, who belatedly understood that his army had been cut off. After some minor engagements that culminated in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ulm" title="Battle of Ulm">Battle of Ulm</a>, Mack finally surrendered after realizing that there was no way to break out of the French encirclement. For just 2,000 French casualties, Napoleon had managed to capture a total of 60,000 Austrian soldiers through his army's rapid marching.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[114]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ulm_Campaign" title="Ulm Campaign">Ulm Campaign</a> is generally regarded as a strategic masterpiece and was influential in the development of the <a href="/wiki/Schlieffen_Plan" title="Schlieffen Plan">Schlieffen Plan</a> in the late 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[115]</a></sup> For the French, this spectacular victory on land was soured by the decisive victory that the Royal Navy attained at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Trafalgar" title="Battle of Trafalgar">Battle of Trafalgar</a> on 21 October. After Trafalgar, Britain had total domination of the seas for the duration of the Napoleonic Wars.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Austerlitz-baron-Pascal.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Austerlitz-baron-Pascal.jpg/300px-Austerlitz-baron-Pascal.jpg" width="300" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Austerlitz-baron-Pascal.jpg/450px-Austerlitz-baron-Pascal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Austerlitz-baron-Pascal.jpg/600px-Austerlitz-baron-Pascal.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="1983" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Austerlitz-baron-Pascal.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Napoleon at the Battle of Austerlitz, by <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_G%C3%A9rard" title="François Gérard">François Gérard</a> 1805. The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Austerlitz" title="Battle of Austerlitz">Battle of Austerlitz</a>, also known as the Battle of the Three Emperors, was one of Napoleon's many victories, where the <a href="/wiki/First_French_Empire" title="First French Empire">French Empire</a> defeated the <a href="/wiki/Third_Coalition" class="mw-redirect" title="Third Coalition">Third Coalition</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following the Ulm Campaign, French forces managed to capture <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> in November. The fall of Vienna provided the French a huge bounty as they captured 100,000 muskets, 500 cannons, and the intact bridges across the <a href="/wiki/Danube_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Danube River">Danube</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[116]</a></sup> At this critical juncture, both <a href="/wiki/Alexander_I_of_Russia" title="Alexander I of Russia">Tsar Alexander I</a> and <a href="/wiki/Francis_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Francis II, Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor Francis II</a> decided to engage Napoleon in battle, despite reservations from some of their subordinates. Napoleon sent his army north in pursuit of the Allies, but then ordered his forces to retreat so that he could feign a grave weakness. Desperate to lure the Allies into battle, Napoleon gave every indication in the days preceding the engagement that the French army was in a pitiful state, even abandoning the dominant Pratzen Heights near the village of Austerlitz. At the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Austerlitz" title="Battle of Austerlitz">Battle of Austerlitz</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Moravia" title="Moravia">Moravia</a> on 2 December, he deployed the French army below the Pratzen Heights and deliberately weakened his right flank, enticing the Allies to launch a major assault there in the hopes of rolling up the whole French line. A forced march from Vienna by <a href="/wiki/Louis-Nicolas_Davout" title="Louis-Nicolas Davout">Marshal Davout</a> and his <a href="/wiki/III_Corps_(Grande_Arm%C3%A9e)" title="III Corps (Grande Armée)">III Corps</a> plugged the gap left by Napoleon just in time. Meanwhile, the heavy Allied deployment against the French right weakened their center on the Pratzen Heights, which was viciously attacked by the <a href="/wiki/IV_Corps_(Grande_Arm%C3%A9e)" title="IV Corps (Grande Armée)">IV Corps</a> of <a href="/wiki/Jean-de-Dieu_Soult" title="Jean-de-Dieu Soult">Marshal Soult</a>. With the Allied center demolished, the French swept through both enemy flanks and sent the Allies fleeing chaotically, capturing thousands of prisoners in the process. The battle is often seen as a tactical masterpiece because of the near-perfect execution of a calibrated but dangerous plan — of the same stature as <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cannae" title="Battle of Cannae">Cannae</a>, the celebrated triumph by <a href="/wiki/Hannibal" title="Hannibal">Hannibal</a> some 2,000 years before.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Allied disaster at Austerlitz significantly shook the faith of Emperor Francis in the British-led war effort. France and Austria agreed to an armistice immediately and the Treaty of Pressburg followed shortly after on 26 December. Pressburg took Austria out of both the war and the Coalition while reinforcing the earlier treaties of <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Campo_Formio" title="Treaty of Campo Formio">Campo Formio</a> and of <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lun%C3%A9ville" title="Treaty of Lunéville">Lunéville</a> between the two powers. The treaty confirmed the Austrian loss of lands to France in <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy_(Napoleonic)" title="Kingdom of Italy (Napoleonic)">Italy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_Bavaria" title="Electorate of Bavaria">Bavaria</a>, and lands in Germany to Napoleon's German allies. It also imposed an indemnity of 40 million francs on the defeated Habsburgs and allowed the fleeing Russian troops free passage through hostile territories and back to their home soil. Napoleon went on to say, "The battle of Austerlitz is the finest of all I have fought".<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[118]</a></sup> Frank McLynn suggests that Napoleon was so successful at Austerlitz that he lost touch with reality, and what used to be French foreign policy became a "personal Napoleonic one".<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[119]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Cronin" title="Vincent Cronin">Vincent Cronin</a> disagrees, stating that Napoleon was not overly ambitious for himself, "he embodied the ambitions of thirty million Frenchmen".<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle-Eastern_alliances">Middle-Eastern alliances</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Franco-Ottoman_alliance" title="Franco-Ottoman alliance">Franco-Ottoman alliance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Franco-Persian_alliance" title="Franco-Persian alliance">Franco-Persian alliance</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Persian_Envoy_Mirza_Mohammed_Reza_Qazvini_Finkenstein_Castle_27_Avril_1807_by_Francois_Mulard.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/The_Persian_Envoy_Mirza_Mohammed_Reza_Qazvini_Finkenstein_Castle_27_Avril_1807_by_Francois_Mulard.jpg/250px-The_Persian_Envoy_Mirza_Mohammed_Reza_Qazvini_Finkenstein_Castle_27_Avril_1807_by_Francois_Mulard.jpg" width="250" height="199" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/The_Persian_Envoy_Mirza_Mohammed_Reza_Qazvini_Finkenstein_Castle_27_Avril_1807_by_Francois_Mulard.jpg/375px-The_Persian_Envoy_Mirza_Mohammed_Reza_Qazvini_Finkenstein_Castle_27_Avril_1807_by_Francois_Mulard.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/The_Persian_Envoy_Mirza_Mohammed_Reza_Qazvini_Finkenstein_Castle_27_Avril_1807_by_Francois_Mulard.jpg/500px-The_Persian_Envoy_Mirza_Mohammed_Reza_Qazvini_Finkenstein_Castle_27_Avril_1807_by_Francois_Mulard.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1127" data-file-height="898" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Persian_Envoy_Mirza_Mohammed_Reza_Qazvini_Finkenstein_Castle_27_Avril_1807_by_Francois_Mulard.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Iranian Envoy Mirza Mohammed Reza-Qazvini meeting with <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleon I">Napoleon I</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Finckenstein_Palace" title="Finckenstein Palace">Finckenstein Palace</a>, 27 April 1807, to sign the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Finckenstein" title="Treaty of Finckenstein">Treaty of Finckenstein</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Napoleon continued to entertain a grand scheme to establish a French presence in the Middle East in order to put pressure on Britain and Russia, and perhaps form an alliance with the Ottoman Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-Watson_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Watson-65">[61]</a></sup> In February 1806, Ottoman Emperor <a href="/wiki/Selim_III" title="Selim III">Selim III</a> finally recognized Napoleon as <i>Emperor</i>. He also opted for an alliance with France, calling France "our sincere and natural ally".<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[121]</a></sup> That decision brought the Ottoman Empire into a losing war against Russia and Britain. A Franco-Persian alliance was also formed between Napoleon and the <a href="/wiki/Qajar_dynasty" title="Qajar dynasty">Persian Empire</a> of <a href="/wiki/Fat%E2%80%B2h-Ali_Shah_Qajar" class="mw-redirect" title="Fat′h-Ali Shah Qajar">Fat′h-Ali Shah Qajar</a>. It collapsed in 1807, when France and Russia themselves formed an unexpected alliance.<sup id="cite_ref-Watson_65-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Watson-65">[61]</a></sup> In the end, Napoleon had made no effective alliances in the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESicker200199_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESicker200199-127">[122]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="War_of_the_Fourth_Coalition_and_Tilsit">War of the Fourth Coalition and Tilsit</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Fourth_Coalition" title="War of the Fourth Coalition">War of the Fourth Coalition</a></div>
<p>After Austerlitz, Napoleon established the <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_the_Rhine" title="Confederation of the Rhine">Confederation of the Rhine</a> in 1806. A collection of German states intended to serve as a buffer zone between France and Central Europe, the creation of the Confederation spelled the end of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> and significantly alarmed the Prussians. The brazen reorganization of German territory by the French risked threatening Prussian influence in the region, if not eliminating it outright. War fever in Berlin rose steadily throughout the summer of 1806. At the insistence of his court, especially his wife <a href="/wiki/Louise_of_Mecklenburg-Strelitz" title="Louise of Mecklenburg-Strelitz">Queen Louise</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frederick_William_III_of_Prussia" title="Frederick William III of Prussia">Frederick William III</a> decided to challenge the French domination of Central Europe by going to war.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[123]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Iena.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Iena.jpg/220px-Iena.jpg" width="220" height="190" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Iena.jpg/330px-Iena.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Iena.jpg/440px-Iena.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="1211" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Iena.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Napoleon reviews the <a href="/wiki/French_Imperial_Guard" class="mw-redirect" title="French Imperial Guard">Imperial Guard</a> before the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Jena" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Jena">Battle of Jena</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The initial military maneuvers began in September 1806. In a letter to <a href="/wiki/Jean-de-Dieu_Soult" title="Jean-de-Dieu Soult">Marshal Soult</a> detailing the plan for the campaign, Napoleon described the essential features of Napoleonic warfare and introduced the phrase <i>le bataillon-carré</i> ("square battalion").<sup id="cite_ref-Chandler_1966.2C_p._467-8_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chandler_1966.2C_p._467-8-129">[124]</a></sup> In the <i>bataillon-carré</i> system, the various corps of the <i>Grande Armée</i> would march uniformly together in close supporting distance.<sup id="cite_ref-Chandler_1966.2C_p._467-8_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chandler_1966.2C_p._467-8-129">[124]</a></sup> If any single corps was attacked, the others could quickly spring into action and arrive to help. Napoleon invaded Prussia with 180,000 troops, rapidly marching on the right bank of the <a href="/wiki/Saale" title="Saale">River Saale</a>. As in previous campaigns, his fundamental objective was to destroy one opponent before reinforcements from another could tip the balance of the war. Upon learning the whereabouts of the Prussian army, the French swung westwards and crossed the Saale with overwhelming force. At the twin <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Jena%E2%80%93Auerstedt" title="Battle of Jena–Auerstedt">battles of Jena and Auerstedt</a>, fought on 14 October, the French convincingly defeated the Prussians and inflicted heavy casualties. With several major commanders dead or incapacitated, the Prussian king proved incapable of effectively commanding the army, which began to quickly disintegrate. In a vaunted pursuit that epitomized the "peak of Napoleonic warfare", according to historian Richard Brooks,<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[125]</a></sup> the French managed to capture 140,000 soldiers, over 2,000 cannons and hundreds of ammunition wagons, all in a single month. Historian David Chandler wrote of the Prussian forces: "Never has the morale of any army been more completely shattered".<sup id="cite_ref-Chandler_1966.2C_p._467-8_129-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chandler_1966.2C_p._467-8-129">[124]</a></sup> Despite their overwhelming defeat, the Prussians refused to negotiate with the French until the Russians had an opportunity to enter the fight.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tilsitz_1807.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Tilsitz_1807.JPG/220px-Tilsitz_1807.JPG" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Tilsitz_1807.JPG/330px-Tilsitz_1807.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Tilsitz_1807.JPG/440px-Tilsitz_1807.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1368" data-file-height="1070" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tilsitz_1807.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_Tilsit" title="Treaties of Tilsit">Treaties of Tilsit</a>: Napoleon meeting with <a href="/wiki/Alexander_I_of_Russia" title="Alexander I of Russia">Alexander I of Russia</a> on a raft in the middle of the <a href="/wiki/Neman_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Neman River">Neman River</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following his triumph, Napoleon imposed the first elements of the Continental System through the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Decree" title="Berlin Decree">Berlin Decree</a> issued in November 1806. The Continental System, which prohibited European nations from trading with Britain, was widely violated throughout his reign.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[127]</a></sup> In the next few months, Napoleon marched against the advancing Russian armies through Poland and was involved in the bloody stalemate at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Eylau" title="Battle of Eylau">Battle of Eylau</a> in February 1807.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[128]</a></sup> After a period of rest and consolidation on both sides, the war restarted in June with an initial struggle at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Heilsberg" title="Battle of Heilsberg">Heilsberg</a> that proved indecisive. On 14 June, however, Napoleon finally obtained an overwhelming victory over the Russians at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Friedland" title="Battle of Friedland">Battle of Friedland</a>, wiping out the majority of the Russian army in a very bloody struggle. The scale of their defeat convinced the Russians to make peace with the French. On 19 June, Czar Alexander sent an envoy to seek an armistice with Napoleon. The latter assured the envoy that the <a href="/wiki/Vistula_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Vistula River">Vistula River</a> represented the natural borders between French and Russian influence in Europe. On that basis, the two emperors began peace negotiations at the town of <a href="/wiki/Sovetsk,_Kaliningrad_Oblast" title="Sovetsk, Kaliningrad Oblast">Tilsit</a> after meeting on an iconic raft on the <a href="/wiki/Neman_(river)" class="mw-redirect" title="Neman (river)">River Niemen</a>. The very first thing Alexander said to Napoleon was probably well-calibrated: "I hate the English as much as you do".<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>Alexander faced pressure from his brother, <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duke_Constantine_Pavlovich_of_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Duke Constantine Pavlovich of Russia">Duke Constantine</a>, to make peace with Napoleon. Given the victory he had just achieved, the French emperor offered the Russians relatively lenient terms–demanding that Russia join the Continental System, withdraw its forces from <a href="/wiki/Wallachia" title="Wallachia">Wallachia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moldavia" title="Moldavia">Moldavia</a>, and hand over the <a href="/wiki/Ionian_Islands" title="Ionian Islands">Ionian Islands</a> to France.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoberts2014458.E2.80.9359_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoberts2014458.E2.80.9359-135">[130]</a></sup> By contrast, Napoleon dictated very harsh peace terms for Prussia, despite the ceaseless exhortations of <a href="/wiki/Louise_of_Mecklenburg-Strelitz" title="Louise of Mecklenburg-Strelitz">Queen Louise</a>. Wiping out half of Prussian territories from the map, Napoleon created a new kingdom of 1,100 square miles called Westphalia. He then appointed his young brother Jérôme as the new monarch of this kingdom. Prussia's humiliating treatment at Tilsit caused a deep and bitter antagonism which festered as the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_era" title="Napoleonic era">Napoleonic era</a> progressed. Moreover, Alexander's pretensions at friendship with Napoleon led the latter to seriously misjudge the true intentions of his Russian counterpart, who would violate numerous provisions of the treaty in the next few years. Despite these problems, the <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_Tilsit" title="Treaties of Tilsit">Treaties of Tilsit</a> at last gave Napoleon a respite from war and allowed him to return to France, which he had not seen in over 300 days.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoberts2014459.E2.80.9361_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoberts2014459.E2.80.9361-136">[131]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Peninsular_War_and_Erfurt">Peninsular War and Erfurt</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">Peninsular War</a></div>
<p>The settlements at Tilsit gave Napoleon time to organize his empire. One of his major objectives became enforcing the Continental System against the British. He decided to focus his attention on the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">Kingdom of Portugal</a>, which consistently violated his trade prohibitions. After defeat in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Oranges" title="War of the Oranges">War of the Oranges</a> in 1801, Portugal adopted a double-sided policy. At first, <a href="/wiki/John_VI_of_Portugal" title="John VI of Portugal">John VI</a> agreed to close his ports to British trade. The situation changed dramatically after the Franco-Spanish defeat at Trafalgar; John grew bolder and officially resumed diplomatic and trade relations with Britain.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Joseph-Bonaparte.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Joseph-Bonaparte.jpg/220px-Joseph-Bonaparte.jpg" width="220" height="326" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Joseph-Bonaparte.jpg/330px-Joseph-Bonaparte.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Joseph-Bonaparte.jpg/440px-Joseph-Bonaparte.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="1037" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Joseph-Bonaparte.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Joseph_Bonaparte" title="Joseph Bonaparte">Joseph Bonaparte</a>, Napoleon's brother, as King of Spain</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Unhappy with this change of policy by the Portuguese government, Napoleon negotiated a <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Fontainebleau_(1807)" title="Treaty of Fontainebleau (1807)">secret treaty</a> with <a href="/wiki/Charles_IV_of_Spain" title="Charles IV of Spain">Charles IV of Spain</a> and sent an army to invade Portugal.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[132]</a></sup> On 17 October 1807, 24,000 French troops under <a href="/wiki/Jean-Andoche_Junot" title="Jean-Andoche Junot">General Junot</a> crossed the <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">Pyrenees</a> with <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Spain">Spanish</a> cooperation and headed towards Portugal to enforce Napoleon's orders.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[133]</a></sup> This attack was the first step in what would eventually become the Peninsular War, a six-year struggle that significantly sapped French strength. Throughout the winter of 1808, French agents became increasingly involved in Spanish internal affairs, attempting to incite discord between members of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Bourbon" title="House of Bourbon">Spanish royal family</a>. On 16 February 1808, secret French machinations finally materialized when Napoleon announced that he would intervene to mediate between the rival political factions in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[134]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Joachim_Murat" title="Joachim Murat">Marshal Murat</a> led 120,000 troops into Spain and the French arrived in <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a> on 24 March,<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[135]</a></sup> where wild riots against the occupation erupted just a few weeks later. Napoleon appointed his brother, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Bonaparte" title="Joseph Bonaparte">Joseph Bonaparte</a>, as the new King of Spain in the summer of 1808. The appointment enraged a heavily religious and conservative Spanish population. Resistance to French aggression soon spread throughout the country. The shocking French defeat at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Bail%C3%A9n" title="Battle of Bailén">Battle of Bailén</a> in July gave hope to Napoleon's enemies and partly persuaded the French emperor to intervene in person.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Before going to Iberia, Napoleon decided to address several lingering issues with the Russians. At the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Erfurt" title="Congress of Erfurt">Congress of Erfurt</a> in October 1808, Napoleon hoped to keep Russia on his side during the upcoming struggle in Spain and during any potential conflict against Austria. The two sides reached an agreement, the Erfurt Convention, that called upon Britain to cease its war against France, that recognized the Russian conquest of <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Finland" title="Grand Duchy of Finland">Finland</a> from <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sweden_(1721%E2%80%931809)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Sweden (1721–1809)">Sweden</a>, and that affirmed Russian support for France in a possible war against Austria "to the best of its ability".<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[136]</a></sup> Napoleon then returned to France and prepared for war. The <i>Grande Armée</i>, under the Emperor's personal command, rapidly crossed the <a href="/wiki/Ebro" title="Ebro">Ebro</a> River in November 1808 and inflicted a series of crushing defeats against the Spanish forces. After clearing the last Spanish force guarding the capital at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Somosierra" title="Battle of Somosierra">Somosierra</a>, Napoleon entered Madrid on 4 December with 80,000 troops.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[137]</a></sup> He then unleashed his soldiers against <a href="/wiki/John_Moore_(British_soldier)" class="mw-redirect" title="John Moore (British soldier)">Moore</a> and the British forces. The British were swiftly driven to the coast, and they withdrew from Spain entirely after a last stand at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Corunna" title="Battle of Corunna">Battle of Corunna</a> in January 1809.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Napoleon would end up leaving Iberia in order to deal with the Austrians in Central Europe, but the Peninsular War continued on long after his absence. He never returned to Spain after the 1808 campaign. Several months after Corunna, the British sent another army to the peninsula under the future <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Wellesley,_1st_Duke_of_Wellington" title="Arthur Wellesley, 1st Duke of Wellington">Duke of Wellington</a>. The war then settled into a complex and asymmetric strategic deadlock where all sides struggled to gain the upper hand. The highlight of the conflict became the brutal <i><a href="/wiki/Guerrilla_warfare" title="Guerrilla warfare">guerrilla warfare</a></i> that engulfed much of the Spanish countryside. Both sides committed the worst atrocities of the Napoleonic Wars during this phase of the conflict. The vicious guerrilla fighting in Spain, largely absent from the French campaigns in Central Europe, severely disrupted the French lines of supply and communication. Although France maintained roughly 300,000 troops in Iberia during the Peninsular War, the vast majority were tied down to garrison duty and to intelligence operations.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[138]</a></sup> The French were never able to concentrate all of their forces effectively, prolonging the war until events elsewhere in Europe finally turned the tide in favor of the Allies. After the invasion of Russia in 1812, the number of French troops in Spain vastly declined as Napoleon needed reinforcements to conserve his strategic position in Europe. By 1814, after scores of battles and sieges throughout Iberia, the Allies had managed to push the French out of the peninsula.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The impact of the Napoleonic invasion of Spain and ousting of the Spanish Bourbon monarchy in favor of his brother Joseph had an enormous impact on the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish empire">Spanish empire</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_America" title="Hispanic America">Spanish America</a> many local elites formed juntas and set up mechanisms to rule in the name of <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_VII_of_Spain" title="Ferdinand VII of Spain">Ferdinand VII of Spain</a>, whom they considered the legitimate Spanish monarch. The outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_American_wars_of_independence" title="Spanish American wars of independence">Spanish American wars of independence</a> in most of the empire was a result of Napoleon's destabilizing actions in Spain and led to the rise of <a href="/wiki/Strongman_(politics)" title="Strongman (politics)">strongmen</a> in the wake of these wars.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[139]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="War_of_the_Fifth_Coalition_and_Marie_Louise">War of the Fifth Coalition and Marie Louise</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Fifth_Coalition" title="War of the Fifth Coalition">War of the Fifth Coalition</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Napoleon_Wagram.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Napoleon_Wagram.jpg/220px-Napoleon_Wagram.jpg" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Napoleon_Wagram.jpg/330px-Napoleon_Wagram.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Napoleon_Wagram.jpg/440px-Napoleon_Wagram.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3154" data-file-height="2326" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Napoleon_Wagram.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Napoleon at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Wagram" title="Battle of Wagram">Battle of Wagram</a>, painted by <a href="/wiki/Horace_Vernet" title="Horace Vernet">Horace Vernet</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After four years on the sidelines, Austria sought another war with France to avenge its recent defeats. Austria could not count on Russian support because the latter was at war with <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Russian_War_(1807%E2%80%931812)" title="Anglo-Russian War (1807–1812)">Britain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finnish_War" title="Finnish War">Sweden</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1806%E2%80%931812)" title="Russo-Turkish War (1806–1812)">Ottoman Empire</a> in 1809. <a href="/wiki/Frederick_William_III_of_Prussia" title="Frederick William III of Prussia">Frederick William</a> of Prussia initially promised to help the Austrians, but reneged before conflict began.<sup id="cite_ref-Fisher_.26_Fremont-Barnes_p._106_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fisher_.26_Fremont-Barnes_p._106-145">[140]</a></sup> A report from the Austrian finance minister suggested that the treasury would run out of money by the middle of 1809 if the large army that the Austrians had formed since the Third Coalition remained mobilized.<sup id="cite_ref-Fisher_.26_Fremont-Barnes_p._106_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fisher_.26_Fremont-Barnes_p._106-145">[140]</a></sup> Although <a href="/wiki/Archduke_Charles,_Duke_of_Teschen" title="Archduke Charles, Duke of Teschen">Archduke Charles</a> warned that the Austrians were not ready for another showdown with Napoleon, a stance that landed him in the so-called "peace party", he did not want to see the army demobilized either.<sup id="cite_ref-Fisher_.26_Fremont-Barnes_p._106_145-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fisher_.26_Fremont-Barnes_p._106-145">[140]</a></sup> On 8 February 1809, the advocates for war finally succeeded when the Imperial Government secretly decided on another confrontation against the French.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In the early morning of 10 April, leading elements of the Austrian army crossed the <a href="/wiki/Inn_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Inn River">Inn River</a> and invaded Bavaria. The early Austrian attack surprised the French; Napoleon himself was still in Paris when he heard about the invasion. He arrived at <a href="/wiki/Donauw%C3%B6rth" title="Donauwörth">Donauwörth</a> on the 17th to find the <i>Grande Armée</i> in a dangerous position, with its two wings separated by 75 miles (121&#160;km) and joined together by a thin cordon of Bavarian troops. Charles pressed the left wing of the French army and hurled his men towards the III Corps of Marshal Davout. In response, Napoleon came up with a plan to cut off the Austrians in the celebrated <i>Landshut Maneuver</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[141]</a></sup> He realigned the axis of his army and marched his soldiers towards the town of <a href="/wiki/Eckm%C3%BChl" title="Eckmühl">Eckmühl</a>. The French scored a convincing win in the resulting <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Eckm%C3%BChl" title="Battle of Eckmühl">Battle of Eckmühl</a>, forcing Charles to withdraw his forces over the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> and into <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a>. On 13 May, Vienna fell for the second time in four years, although the war continued since most of the Austrian army had survived the initial engagements in Southern Germany.</p>
<p>By 17 May, the main Austrian army under Charles had arrived on the Marchfeld. Charles kept the bulk of his troops several miles away from the river bank in hopes of concentrating them at the point where Napoleon decided to cross. On 21 May, the French made their first major effort to cross the Danube, precipitating the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Aspern-Essling" title="Battle of Aspern-Essling">Battle of Aspern-Essling</a>. The Austrians enjoyed a comfortable numerical superiority over the French throughout the battle; on the first day, Charles disposed of 110,000 soldiers against only 31,000 commanded by Napoleon.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[142]</a></sup> By the second day, reinforcements had boosted French numbers up to 70,000.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[143]</a></sup> The battle was characterized by a vicious back-and-forth struggle for the two villages of Aspern and Essling, the focal points of the French bridgehead. By the end of the fighting, the French had lost Aspern but still controlled Essling. A sustained Austrian artillery bombardment eventually convinced Napoleon to withdraw his forces back onto Lobau Island. Both sides inflicted about 23,000 casualties on each other.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[144]</a></sup> It was the first defeat Napoleon suffered in a major set-piece battle, and it caused excitement throughout many parts of Europe because it proved that he could be beaten on the battlefield.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[145]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the setback at Aspern-Essling, Napoleon took more than six weeks in planning and preparing for contingencies before he made another attempt at crossing the Danube.<sup id="cite_ref-David_G._Chandler_p._708_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-David_G._Chandler_p._708-151">[146]</a></sup> From 30 June to the early days of July, the French recrossed the Danube in strength, with more than 180,000 troops marching across the Marchfeld towards the Austrians.<sup id="cite_ref-David_G._Chandler_p._708_151-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-David_G._Chandler_p._708-151">[146]</a></sup> Charles received the French with 150,000 of his own men.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[147]</a></sup> In the ensuing <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Wagram" title="Battle of Wagram">Battle of Wagram</a>, which also lasted two days, Napoleon commanded his forces in what was the largest battle of his career up until then. Napoleon finished off the battle with a concentrated central thrust that punctured a hole in the Austrian army and forced Charles to retreat. Austrian losses were very heavy, reaching well over 40,000 casualties.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[148]</a></sup> The French were too exhausted to pursue the Austrians immediately, but Napoleon eventually caught up with Charles at <a href="/wiki/Znojmo" title="Znojmo">Znaim</a> and the latter signed an <a href="/wiki/Armistice_of_Znaim" title="Armistice of Znaim">armistice</a> on 12 July.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Napoleoniceurope.png" class="image"><img alt="Map of Europe. French Empire shown as bigger than present day France as it included parts of present-day Netherlands and Italy." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Napoleoniceurope.png/220px-Napoleoniceurope.png" width="220" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Napoleoniceurope.png/330px-Napoleoniceurope.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d8/Napoleoniceurope.png 2x" data-file-width="415" data-file-height="422" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Napoleoniceurope.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/First_French_Empire" title="First French Empire">First French Empire</a> at its greatest extent in 1811
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #000090; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;French Empire</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #3340dd; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;French <a href="/wiki/Satellite_state" title="Satellite state">satellite states</a></div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #27c600; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Allied states</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Holland" title="Kingdom of Holland">Kingdom of Holland</a>, the British launched the <a href="/wiki/Walcheren_Campaign" title="Walcheren Campaign">Walcheren Campaign</a> to open up a second front in the war and to relieve the pressure on the Austrians. The British army only landed at <a href="/wiki/Walcheren" title="Walcheren">Walcheren</a> on 30 July, by which point the Austrians had already been defeated. The Walcheren Campaign was characterized by little fighting but heavy casualties thanks to the popularly dubbed "<a href="/wiki/Walcheren_Fever" class="mw-redirect" title="Walcheren Fever">Walcheren Fever</a>". Over 4000 British troops were lost in a bungled campaign, and the rest withdrew in December 1809.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[149]</a></sup> The main strategic result from the campaign became the delayed political settlement between the French and the Austrians. Emperor Francis wanted to wait and see how the British performed in their theater before entering into negotiations with Napoleon. Once it became apparent that the British were going nowhere, the Austrians agreed to peace talks.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The resulting <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Sch%C3%B6nbrunn" title="Treaty of Schönbrunn">Treaty of Schönbrunn</a> in October 1809 was the harshest that France had imposed on Austria in recent memory. <a href="/wiki/Klemens_Wenzel_von_Metternich" class="mw-redirect" title="Klemens Wenzel von Metternich">Metternich</a> and Archduke Charles had the preservation of the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Habsburg Empire">Habsburg Empire</a> as their fundamental goal, and to this end they succeeded by making Napoleon seek more modest goals in return for promises of friendship between the two powers.<sup id="cite_ref-Todd_Fisher_p._144_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Todd_Fisher_p._144-155">[150]</a></sup> Nevertheless, while most of the hereditary lands remained a part of the Habsburg realm, France received <a href="/wiki/Carinthia_(province)" class="mw-redirect" title="Carinthia (province)">Carinthia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carniola" title="Carniola">Carniola</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">Adriatic</a> ports, while <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Central_Europe)" class="mw-redirect" title="Galicia (Central Europe)">Galicia</a> was given to the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Warsaw" title="Duchy of Warsaw">Poles</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Salzburg" title="Salzburg">Salzburg</a> area of the <a href="/wiki/County_of_Tyrol" title="County of Tyrol">Tyrol</a> went to the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bavaria" title="Kingdom of Bavaria">Bavarians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Todd_Fisher_p._144_155-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Todd_Fisher_p._144-155">[150]</a></sup> Austria lost over three million subjects, about one-fifth of her total population, as a result of these territorial changes.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[151]</a></sup> Although fighting in Iberia continued, the War of the Fifth Coalition would be the last major conflict on the European continent for the next three years.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Napoleon turned his focus to domestic affairs after the war. <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9phine_de_Beauharnais" title="Joséphine de Beauharnais">Empress Joséphine</a> had still not given birth to a child from Napoleon, who became worried about the future of his empire following his death. Desperate for a legitimate heir, Napoleon divorced Joséphine in January 1810 and started looking for a new wife. Hoping to cement the recent alliance with Austria through a family connection, Napoleon married the <a href="/wiki/Marie_Louise,_Duchess_of_Parma" title="Marie Louise, Duchess of Parma">Archduchess Marie Louise</a>, who was 18 years old at the time. On 20 March 1811, Marie Louise gave birth to a baby boy, whom Napoleon made heir apparent and bestowed the title of <i><a href="/wiki/King_of_the_Romans" title="King of the Romans">King of Rome</a></i>. His son never actually ruled the empire, but historians still refer to him as <i><a href="/wiki/Napoleon_II" title="Napoleon II">Napoleon II</a></i>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Invasion_of_Russia">Invasion of Russia</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/French_invasion_of_Russia" title="French invasion of Russia">French invasion of Russia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Napoleon_Moscow_Fire.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Napoleon_Moscow_Fire.JPG/220px-Napoleon_Moscow_Fire.JPG" width="220" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Napoleon_Moscow_Fire.JPG/330px-Napoleon_Moscow_Fire.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Napoleon_Moscow_Fire.JPG/440px-Napoleon_Moscow_Fire.JPG 2x" data-file-width="707" data-file-height="602" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Napoleon_Moscow_Fire.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Fire_of_Moscow_(1812)" title="Fire of Moscow (1812)">Moscow fire</a> depicted by an unknown German artist</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1808, Napoleon and Czar Alexander met at the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Erfurt" title="Congress of Erfurt">Congress of Erfurt</a> to preserve the Russo-French alliance. The leaders had a friendly personal relationship after their first meeting at Tilsit in 1807.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[152]</a></sup> By 1811, however, tensions had increased and Alexander was under pressure from the <a href="/wiki/Russian_nobility" title="Russian nobility">Russian nobility</a> to break off the alliance. A major strain on the relationship between the two nations became the regular violations of the Continental System by the Russians, which led Napoleon to threaten Alexander with serious consequences if he formed an alliance with Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[153]</a></sup></p>
<p>By 1812, advisers to Alexander suggested the possibility of an invasion of the French Empire and the recapture of Poland. On receipt of intelligence reports on Russia's war preparations, Napoleon expanded his <i>Grande Armée</i> to more than 450,000 men.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[154]</a></sup> He ignored repeated advice against an invasion of the Russian heartland and prepared for an offensive campaign; on 24 June 1812 the invasion commenced.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[155]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Napoleons_retreat_from_moscow.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Napoleons_retreat_from_moscow.jpg/220px-Napoleons_retreat_from_moscow.jpg" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Napoleons_retreat_from_moscow.jpg/330px-Napoleons_retreat_from_moscow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Napoleons_retreat_from_moscow.jpg/440px-Napoleons_retreat_from_moscow.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="570" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Napoleons_retreat_from_moscow.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Napoleon's withdrawal from Russia</i>, a painting by <a href="/wiki/Adolph_Northen" title="Adolph Northen">Adolph Northen</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In an attempt to gain increased support from Polish nationalists and patriots, Napoleon termed the war the <i>Second Polish War</i>—the <i>First Polish War</i> had been the <a href="/wiki/Bar_Confederation" title="Bar Confederation">Bar Confederation</a> uprising by Polish nobles against Russia in 1768. Polish patriots wanted the Russian part of Poland to be joined with the Duchy of Warsaw and an independent Poland created. This was rejected by Napoleon, who stated he had promised his ally Austria this would not happen. Napoleon refused to <a href="/wiki/Manumission" title="Manumission">manumit</a> the Russian <a href="/wiki/Serf" class="mw-redirect" title="Serf">serfs</a> because of concerns this might provoke a reaction in his army's rear. The serfs later committed atrocities against French soldiers during France's retreat.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[156]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Russians avoided Napoleon's objective of a decisive engagement and instead retreated deeper into Russia. A brief attempt at resistance was made at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Smolensk_(1812)" title="Battle of Smolensk (1812)">Smolensk</a> in August; the Russians were defeated in a series of battles, and Napoleon resumed his advance. The Russians again avoided battle, although in a few cases this was only achieved because Napoleon uncharacteristically hesitated to attack when the opportunity arose. Owing to the Russian army's <a href="/wiki/Scorched_earth" title="Scorched earth">scorched earth</a> tactics, the French found it increasingly difficult to forage food for themselves and their horses.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[157]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Russians eventually offered battle outside Moscow on 7 September: the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Borodino" title="Battle of Borodino">Battle of Borodino</a> resulted in approximately 44,000 Russian and 35,000 French dead, wounded or captured, and may have been the bloodiest day of battle in history up to that point in time.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[158]</a></sup> Although the French had won, the Russian army had accepted, and withstood, the major battle Napoleon had hoped would be decisive. Napoleon's own account was: "The most terrible of all my battles was the one before Moscow. The French showed themselves to be worthy of victory, but the Russians showed themselves worthy of being invincible".<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[159]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Russian army withdrew and retreated past Moscow. Napoleon entered the city, assuming its fall would end the war and Alexander would negotiate peace. However, on orders of the city's governor <a href="/wiki/Feodor_Rostopchin" class="mw-redirect" title="Feodor Rostopchin">Feodor Rostopchin</a>, rather than capitulation, Moscow was burned. After five weeks, Napoleon and his army left. In early November Napoleon got concerned about loss of control back in France after the <a href="/wiki/Malet_coup_of_1812" title="Malet coup of 1812">Malet coup of 1812</a>. His army walked through snow up to their knees and nearly 10,000 men and horses froze to death on the night of 8/9 November alone. After the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Berezina" title="Battle of Berezina">Battle of Berezina</a> Napoleon managed to escape but had to abandon much of the remaining artillery and baggage train. On 5 December, shortly before arriving in Vilnius, Napoleon left the army in a sledge.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[160]</a></sup></p>
<p>The French suffered in the course of a ruinous retreat, including from the harshness of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Winter" title="Russian Winter">Russian Winter</a>. The Armée had begun as over 400,000 frontline troops, with fewer than 40,000 crossing the <a href="/wiki/Berezina_River" title="Berezina River">Berezina River</a> in November 1812.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[161]</a></sup> The Russians had lost 150,000 in battle and hundreds of thousands of civilians.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[162]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="War_of_the_Sixth_Coalition">War of the Sixth Coalition</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Sixth_Coalition" title="War of the Sixth Coalition">War of the Sixth Coalition</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Montfort_-_Adieux_de_Napoleon_a_la_Garde_imperiale.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Montfort_-_Adieux_de_Napoleon_a_la_Garde_imperiale.jpg/220px-Montfort_-_Adieux_de_Napoleon_a_la_Garde_imperiale.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Montfort_-_Adieux_de_Napoleon_a_la_Garde_imperiale.jpg/330px-Montfort_-_Adieux_de_Napoleon_a_la_Garde_imperiale.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Montfort_-_Adieux_de_Napoleon_a_la_Garde_imperiale.jpg/440px-Montfort_-_Adieux_de_Napoleon_a_la_Garde_imperiale.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1370" data-file-height="1013" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Montfort_-_Adieux_de_Napoleon_a_la_Garde_imperiale.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Napoleon's farewell to his Imperial Guard, 20 April 1814</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There was a lull in fighting over the winter of 1812–13 while both the Russians and the French rebuilt their forces; Napoleon was able to field 350,000 troops.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[163]</a></sup> Heartened by France's loss in Russia, Prussia joined with Austria, Sweden, Russia, Great Britain, Spain, and Portugal in a new coalition. Napoleon assumed command in Germany and inflicted a series of defeats on the Coalition culminating in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Dresden" title="Battle of Dresden">Battle of Dresden</a> in August 1813.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[164]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite these successes, the numbers continued to mount against Napoleon, and the French army was pinned down by a force twice its size and lost at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Leipzig" title="Battle of Leipzig">Battle of Leipzig</a>. This was by far the largest battle of the Napoleonic Wars and cost more than 90,000 casualties in total.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[165]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Allies offered peace terms in the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_proposals" title="Frankfurt proposals">Frankfurt proposals</a> in November 1813. Napoleon would remain as Emperor of France, but it would be reduced to its "natural frontiers". That meant that France could retain control of Belgium, Savoy and the Rhineland (the west bank of the Rhine River), while giving up control of all the rest, including all of Spain and the Netherlands, and most of Italy and Germany. Metternich told Napoleon these were the best terms the Allies were likely to offer; after further victories, the terms would be harsher and harsher. Metternich's motivation was to maintain France as a balance against Russian threats, while ending the highly destabilizing series of wars.<sup id="cite_ref-J._P._Riley_2013_206_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-J._P._Riley_2013_206-171">[166]</a></sup></p>
<p>Napoleon, expecting to win the war, delayed too long and lost this opportunity; by December the Allies had withdrawn the offer. When his back was to the wall in 1814 he tried to reopen peace negotiations on the basis of accepting the Frankfurt proposals. The Allies now had new, harsher terms that included the retreat of France to its 1791 boundaries, which meant the loss of Belgium. Napoleon would remain Emperor, however he rejected the term. The British wanted Napoleon permanently removed; they prevailed. Napoleon adamantly refused.<sup id="cite_ref-J._P._Riley_2013_206_171-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-J._P._Riley_2013_206-171">[166]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[167]</a></sup></p>
<p>Napoleon withdrew back into France, his army reduced to 70,000 soldiers, and little cavalry; he faced more than three times as many Allied troops.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[168]</a></sup> The French were surrounded: British armies pressed from the south, and other Coalition forces positioned to attack from the German states. Napoleon won a series of victories in the <a href="/wiki/Six_Days%27_Campaign" title="Six Days' Campaign">Six Days' Campaign</a>, though these were not significant enough to turn the tide. The leaders of Paris surrendered to the Coalition in March 1814.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[169]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DelarocheNapoleon.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/DelarocheNapoleon.jpg/220px-DelarocheNapoleon.jpg" width="220" height="292" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/DelarocheNapoleon.jpg/330px-DelarocheNapoleon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/DelarocheNapoleon.jpg/440px-DelarocheNapoleon.jpg 2x" data-file-width="602" data-file-height="800" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DelarocheNapoleon.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Napoleon abdicated in Fontainebleau, 4 April 1814, by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Delaroche" title="Paul Delaroche">Paul Delaroche</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 1 April, Alexander addressed the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9nat_conservateur" title="Sénat conservateur">Sénat conservateur</a>. Long docile to Napoleon, under Talleyrand's prodding it had turned against him. Alexander told the Sénat that the Allies were fighting against Napoleon, not France, and they were prepared to offer honorable peace terms if Napoleon were removed from power. The next day, the Sénat passed the <a href="/wiki/Acte_de_d%C3%A9ch%C3%A9ance_de_l%27Empereur" title="Acte de déchéance de l'Empereur">Acte de déchéance de l'Empereur</a> ("Emperor's Demise Act"), which declared Napoleon deposed. Napoleon had advanced as far as <a href="/wiki/Fontainebleau" title="Fontainebleau">Fontainebleau</a> when he learned that Paris was lost. When Napoleon proposed the army march on the capital, his senior officers and marshals mutinied.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGates2003259_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGates2003259-175">[170]</a></sup> On 4 April, led by <a href="/wiki/Michel_Ney" title="Michel Ney">Ney</a>, they confronted Napoleon. Napoleon asserted the army would follow him, and Ney replied the army would follow its generals. While the ordinary soldiers and regimental officers wanted to fight on, without any senior officers or marshals any prospective invasion of Paris would have been impossible. Bowing to the inevitable, on 4 April Napoleon abdicated in favour of his son, with Marie Louise as regent. However, the Allies refused to accept this under prodding from Alexander, who feared that Napoleon might find an excuse to retake the throne.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[171]</a></sup> Napoleon was then forced to announce his unconditional abdication only two days later.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Exile_to_Elba">Exile to Elba</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Napoleon%27s_exile_to_Elba3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Cartoon of Napoleon sitting back to front on a donkey with a broken sword and two soldiers in the background drumming" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Napoleon%27s_exile_to_Elba3.jpg/220px-Napoleon%27s_exile_to_Elba3.jpg" width="220" height="181" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Napoleon%27s_exile_to_Elba3.jpg/330px-Napoleon%27s_exile_to_Elba3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Napoleon%27s_exile_to_Elba3.jpg/440px-Napoleon%27s_exile_to_Elba3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3545" data-file-height="2910" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Napoleon%27s_exile_to_Elba3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
British etching from 1814 in celebration of Napoleon's first exile to Elba at the close of the War of the Sixth Coalition</div>
</div>
</div>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>The Allied Powers having declared that Emperor Napoleon was the sole obstacle to the restoration of peace in Europe, Emperor Napoleon, faithful to his oath, declares that he renounces, for himself and his heirs, the thrones of France and Italy, and that there is no personal sacrifice, even that of his life, which he is not ready to do in the interests of France.<br />
Done in the palace of Fontainebleau, 11 April 1814.</p>
<div class="templatequotecite"><cite>— Act of abdication of Napoleon<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[172]</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Fontainebleau_(1814)" title="Treaty of Fontainebleau (1814)">Treaty of Fontainebleau</a>, the Allies exiled him to <a href="/wiki/Elba" title="Elba">Elba</a>, an island of 12,000 inhabitants in the Mediterranean, 20&#160;km (12&#160;mi) off the <a href="/wiki/Tuscany" title="Tuscany">Tuscan</a> coast. They gave him sovereignty over the island and allowed him to retain the title of <i>Emperor</i>. Napoleon attempted suicide with a pill he had carried after nearly being captured by the Russians during the retreat from Moscow. Its potency had weakened with age, however, and he survived to be exiled while his wife and son took refuge in Austria.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[173]</a></sup> In the first few months on Elba he created a small navy and army, developed the iron mines, oversaw the construction of new roads, issued decrees on modern agricultural methods, and overhauled the island's legal and educational system.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[175]</a></sup></p>
<p>A few months into his exile, Napoleon learned that his ex-wife Josephine had died in France. He was devastated by the news, locking himself in his room and refusing to leave for two days.<sup id="cite_ref-pbs.org_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbs.org-181">[176]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hundred_Days">Hundred Days</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Days" title="Hundred Days">Hundred Days</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Retour_de_Napoleon_d%27_Isle_d%27Elbe,_by_Charles_de_Steuben.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Retour_de_Napoleon_d%27_Isle_d%27Elbe%2C_by_Charles_de_Steuben.jpg/220px-Retour_de_Napoleon_d%27_Isle_d%27Elbe%2C_by_Charles_de_Steuben.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Retour_de_Napoleon_d%27_Isle_d%27Elbe%2C_by_Charles_de_Steuben.jpg/330px-Retour_de_Napoleon_d%27_Isle_d%27Elbe%2C_by_Charles_de_Steuben.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Retour_de_Napoleon_d%27_Isle_d%27Elbe%2C_by_Charles_de_Steuben.jpg/440px-Retour_de_Napoleon_d%27_Isle_d%27Elbe%2C_by_Charles_de_Steuben.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1574" data-file-height="1177" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Retour_de_Napoleon_d%27_Isle_d%27Elbe,_by_Charles_de_Steuben.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Napoleon returned from Elba, by Karl Stenben, 19th century</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Separated from his wife and son, who had returned to Austria, cut off from the allowance guaranteed to him by the Treaty of Fontainebleau, and aware of rumours he was about to be banished to a remote island in the Atlantic Ocean,<sup id="cite_ref-Mclynn604_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mclynn604-182">[177]</a></sup> Napoleon escaped from Elba, in the <a href="/wiki/Brig" title="Brig">brig</a> <a href="/wiki/French_brig_Inconstant_(1811)" title="French brig Inconstant (1811)"><i>Inconstant</i></a> on 26 February 1815 with 700 men.<sup id="cite_ref-Mclynn604_182-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mclynn604-182">[177]</a></sup> Two days later, he landed on the French mainland at <a href="/wiki/Golfe-Juan" title="Golfe-Juan">Golfe-Juan</a> and started heading north.<sup id="cite_ref-Mclynn604_182-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mclynn604-182">[177]</a></sup></p>
<p>The 5th Regiment was sent to intercept him and made contact <a href="/wiki/Route_Napol%C3%A9on" title="Route Napoléon">just south</a> of <a href="/wiki/Grenoble" title="Grenoble">Grenoble</a> on 7 March 1815. Napoleon approached the regiment alone, dismounted his horse and, when he was within gunshot range, shouted to the soldiers, "Here I am. Kill your Emperor, if you wish".<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[178]</a></sup> The soldiers quickly responded with, "Vive L'Empereur!" Ney, who had boasted to the restored Bourbon king, <a href="/wiki/Louis_XVIII_of_France" title="Louis XVIII of France">Louis XVIII</a>, that he would bring Napoleon to Paris in an iron cage, affectionately kissed his former emperor and forgot his oath of allegiance to the Bourbon monarch. The two then marched together towards Paris with a growing army. The unpopular Louis XVIII fled to Belgium after realizing he had little political support. On 13 March, the powers at the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Congress of Vienna</a> declared Napoleon an <a href="/wiki/Outlaw" title="Outlaw">outlaw</a>. Four days later, Great Britain, Russia, Austria, and Prussia each pledged to put 150,000 men into the field to end his rule.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[179]</a></sup></p>
<p>Napoleon arrived in Paris on 20 March and governed for a period now called the Hundred Days. By the start of June the armed forces available to him had reached 200,000, and he decided to go on the offensive to attempt to drive a wedge between the oncoming British and Prussian armies. The French Army of the North crossed the frontier into the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="United Kingdom of the Netherlands">United Kingdom of the Netherlands</a>, in modern-day Belgium.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[180]</a></sup></p>
<p>Napoleon's forces fought the Coalition armies, commanded by the <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Wellesley,_1st_Duke_of_Wellington" title="Arthur Wellesley, 1st Duke of Wellington">Duke of Wellington</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gebhard_Leberecht_von_Bl%C3%BCcher" title="Gebhard Leberecht von Blücher">Gebhard Leberecht von Blücher</a>, at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Waterloo" title="Battle of Waterloo">Battle of Waterloo</a> on 18 June 1815. Wellington's army withstood repeated attacks by the French and drove them from the field while the Prussians arrived in force and broke through Napoleon's right flank.</p>
<p>Napoleon returned to Paris and found that both the legislature and the people had turned against him.
