After her wedding, she wrote to her father "He loves me very much. I respond to his love sincerely. There is something very fetching and very eager about him that is impossible to resist".<sup id="cite_ref-pbs.org_181-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbs.org-181">[176]</a></sup></p>
<p>Napoleon and Marie Louise remained married until his death, though she did not join him in exile on Elba and thereafter never saw her husband again. The couple had one child, <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_II" title="Napoleon II">Napoleon Francis Joseph Charles</a> (1811–1832), known from birth as the <a href="/wiki/King_of_the_Romans" title="King of the Romans">King of Rome</a>. He became Napoleon II in 1814 and reigned for only two weeks. He was awarded the title of the Duke of Reichstadt in 1818 and died of <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> aged 21, with no children.<sup id="cite_ref-McLynn_1998.2C_p.663_285-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McLynn_1998.2C_p.663-285">[277]</a></sup></p>
<p>Napoleon acknowledged one illegitimate son: <a href="/wiki/Charles_L%C3%A9on" title="Charles Léon">Charles Léon</a> (1806–1881) by <a href="/wiki/El%C3%A9onore_Denuelle_de_La_Plaigne" title="Eléonore Denuelle de La Plaigne">Eléonore Denuelle de La Plaigne</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-m630_286-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-m630-286">[278]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alexandre_Colonna-Walewski" title="Alexandre Colonna-Walewski">Alexandre Colonna-Walewski</a> (1810–1868), the son of his mistress <a href="/wiki/Maria_Walewska" class="mw-redirect" title="Maria Walewska">Maria Walewska</a>, although acknowledged by Walewska's husband, was also widely known to be his child, and the DNA of his direct male descendant has been used to help confirm Napoleon's <a href="/wiki/Haplotype#Y-DNA_haplotypes_from_genealogical_DNA_tests" title="Haplotype">Y-chromosome haplotype</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">[279]</a></sup> He may have had further unacknowledged illegitimate offspring as well, such as <a href="/w/index.php?title=Eugen_Megerle_von_M%C3%BChlfeld&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Eugen Megerle von Mühlfeld (page does not exist)">Eugen Megerle von Mühlfeld</a> by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Emilie_Victoria_Kraus_von_Wolfsberg&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Emilie Victoria Kraus von Wolfsberg (page does not exist)">Emilie Victoria Kraus</a><sup id="cite_ref-McLynn423_288-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McLynn423-288">[280]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/H%C3%A9l%C3%A8ne_Napoleone_Bonaparte" title="Hélène Napoleone Bonaparte">Hélène Napoleone Bonaparte</a> (1816–1907) by <a href="/wiki/Albine_de_Montholon" title="Albine de Montholon">Albine de Montholon</a>.</p>
<h2><span id="Titles,_styles,_honours,_and_arms"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Titles.2C_styles.2C_honours.2C_and_arms">Titles, styles, honours, and arms</span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/File:Portal-puzzle.svg" class="image"><img alt="Portal-puzzle.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fd/Portal-puzzle.svg/32px-Portal-puzzle.svg.png" width="32" height="28" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fd/Portal-puzzle.svg/48px-Portal-puzzle.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fd/Portal-puzzle.svg/64px-Portal-puzzle.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="32" data-file-height="28" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Corsica" class="mw-redirect" title="Portal:Corsica">Corsica portal</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 35em; -webkit-column-width: 35em; column-width: 35em; list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-13">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">He established a system of public education,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrab200356_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrab200356-7">[7]</a></sup> abolished the vestiges of <a href="/wiki/Feudalism" title="Feudalism">feudalism</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Broers_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Broers-8">[8]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_and_the_Jews" title="Napoleon and the Jews">emancipated Jews</a> and other religious minorities,<sup id="cite_ref-Conner_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Conner-9">[9]</a></sup> abolished the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Inquisition" title="Spanish Inquisition">Spanish Inquisition</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-JosephPerez_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JosephPerez-10">[10]</a></sup> enacted <a href="/wiki/Equality_before_the_law" title="Equality before the law">legal protections</a> for an emerging middle class,<sup id="cite_ref-FisherBarnes_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FisherBarnes-11">[11]</a></sup> and centralized state power at the expense of religious authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">His name was also spelled as <i>Nabulione</i>, <i>Nabulio</i>, <i>Napolionne</i>, and <i>Napulione</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-dwyerxv_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dwyerxv-16">[15]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-28"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-28">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Aside from his name, there does not appear to be a connection between him and <a href="/wiki/Napoleon%27s_theorem" title="Napoleon's theorem">Napoleon's theorem</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[25]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-32"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-32">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">He was mainly referred to as Bonaparte until he became First Consul for life.<sup id="cite_ref-m290_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-m290-31">[28]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-86"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-86">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This is depicted in <i><a href="/wiki/Bonaparte_Crossing_the_Alps" title="Bonaparte Crossing the Alps">Bonaparte Crossing the Alps</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Hippolyte_Delaroche" class="mw-redirect" title="Hippolyte Delaroche">Hippolyte Delaroche</a> and in Jacques-Louis David's imperial <i>Napoleon Crossing the Alps</i>. He is less realistically portrayed on a <a href="/wiki/Horses_in_warfare" title="Horses in warfare">charger</a> in the latter work.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[81]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-196"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-196">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">It was customary to cast a death mask of a leader. At least four genuine death masks of Napoleon are known to exist: one in <a href="/wiki/The_Cabildo" title="The Cabildo">The Cabildo</a> in New Orleans, one in a Liverpool museum, another in Havana and one in the library of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Carolina" title="University of North Carolina">University of North Carolina</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[190]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-203"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-203">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The body can tolerate large doses of arsenic if ingested regularly, and arsenic was a fashionable <a href="/wiki/Panacea_(medicine)" title="Panacea (medicine)">cure-all</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[196]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-283"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-283">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">One night, during an illicit liaison with the actress Marguerite George, Napoleon had a major fit. This and other more minor attacks have led historians to debate whether he had epilepsy and, if so, to what extent.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">[275]</a></sup></span></li>
</ol>
</div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biographical_studies">Biographical studies</span></h3>
